Council</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Portsmouth</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;p&#39; in &#39;pie&#39;">p</span><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;war&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="/\xce\xb8/: &#39;th&#39; in &#39;thigh&#39;">\xce\xb8</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-uk-Portsmouth.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/27/En-uk-Portsmouth.ogg" class="internal" title="En-uk-Portsmouth.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">port</a> <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">Hampshire</a>, England, with a total population of 205,400 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-Population_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BUA_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BUA-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The city of Portsmouth is nicknamed <i><b>Pompey</b></i> and is mainly built on <a href="/wiki/Portsea_Island" title="Portsea Island">Portsea Island</a>, a flat, low-lying island measuring 24 square kilometres (9 sq mi) in area, just off the south-east coast of Hampshire. Uniquely, Portsmouth is the only island city in the United Kingdom<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>, and is the only city whose <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_districts_by_population_density" title="List of English districts by population density">population density</a> exceeds that of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Population_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201316_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201316-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Portsmouth is located 70 miles (110&#160;km) south-west of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and 19 miles (31&#160;km) south-east of <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a>. With the surrounding towns of <a href="/wiki/Gosport" title="Gosport">Gosport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fareham" title="Fareham">Fareham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Havant" title="Havant">Havant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waterlooville" title="Waterlooville">Waterlooville</a>, Portsmouth forms the eastern half of the <a href="/wiki/South_Hampshire" title="South Hampshire">South Hampshire metropolitan area</a>, which includes Southampton and <a href="/wiki/Eastleigh" title="Eastleigh">Eastleigh</a> in the western half.\n</p><p>Portsmouth\'s history can be traced back to <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman times</a>. A significant naval port for centuries, Portsmouth has the world\'s oldest <a href="/wiki/Dry_dock" title="Dry dock">dry dock</a>. In the sixteenth century, Portsmouth was England\'s first line of defence during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Solent" title="Battle of the Solent">French invasion</a> of 1545. By the early nineteenth century, the world\'s first mass <a href="/wiki/Production_line" title="Production line">production line</a> was set up in Portsmouth Dockyard\'s <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Block_Mills" title="Portsmouth Block Mills">Block Mills</a>, making it the most industrialised site in the world and birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>. Portsmouth was also the most heavily <a href="/wiki/Fortification" title="Fortification">fortified</a> town in the world, and was considered "the world\'s greatest naval port" at the height of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> throughout <i><a href="/wiki/Pax_Britannica" title="Pax Britannica">Pax Britannica</a></i>. Defences known as the <a href="/wiki/Palmerston_Forts,_Portsmouth" title="Palmerston Forts, Portsmouth">Palmerston Forts</a> were built around Portsmouth in 1859 in anticipation of another invasion from continental Europe.\n</p><p>In 1926, Portsmouth was officially elevated in status from a <a href="/wiki/List_of_towns_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of towns in the United Kingdom">town</a> to a <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city</a>. The motto "<i>Heaven\'s Light Our Guide</i>" was registered to the City of Portsmouth in 1929.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, the city of Portsmouth was a pivotal embarkation point for the <a href="/wiki/D-Day_landings" class="mw-redirect" title="D-Day landings">D-Day landings</a> and was bombed extensively in the <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Blitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Portsmouth Blitz">Portsmouth Blitz</a>, which resulted in the deaths of 930 people. In 1982, a large proportion of the task force dispatched to liberate the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> deployed from the city\'s naval base. <a href="/wiki/HMY_Britannia" title="HMY Britannia">Her Majesty\'s Yacht <i>Britannia</i></a> left the city to oversee the <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_sovereignty_over_Hong_Kong" class="mw-redirect" title="Transfer of sovereignty over Hong Kong">transfer of Hong Kong</a> in 1997, which marked for many the end of the empire. In 1997, Portsmouth became a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authorities_of_England" title="Unitary authorities of England">Unitary Authority</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_City_Council" title="Portsmouth City Council">Portsmouth City Council</a> gaining powers of a non-metropolitan county and district council combined, responsibilities previously held by <a href="/wiki/Hampshire_County_Council" title="Hampshire County Council">Hampshire County Council</a>.\n</p><p>Portsmouth is one of the world\'s best known ports. <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Portsmouth" title="HMNB Portsmouth">HMNB Portsmouth</a> is considered to be the home of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> and is home to two-thirds of the UK\'s surface fleet. The city is home to some famous ships, including <a href="/wiki/HMS_Warrior_(1860)" title="HMS Warrior (1860)">HMS <i>Warrior</i></a>, the Tudor <a href="/wiki/Carrack" title="Carrack">carrack</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_Rose" title="Mary Rose">Mary Rose</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Nelson,_1st_Viscount_Nelson" title="Horatio Nelson, 1st Viscount Nelson">Horatio Nelson\'s</a> flagship, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Victory" title="HMS Victory">HMS <i>Victory</i></a> (the world\'s oldest naval ship still in commission). The former <a href="/wiki/HMS_Vernon_(shore_establishment)" title="HMS Vernon (shore establishment)">HMS <i>Vernon</i> naval shore establishment</a> has been redeveloped as a retail park known as <a href="/wiki/Gunwharf_Quays" title="Gunwharf Quays">Gunwharf Quays</a>. Portsmouth is among the few British cities with two cathedrals: the <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Cathedral" title="Portsmouth Cathedral">Anglican Cathedral of St Thomas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_St_John_the_Evangelist,_Portsmouth" title="Cathedral of St John the Evangelist, Portsmouth">Cathedral of St John the Evangelist</a>. The waterfront and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Harbour" title="Portsmouth Harbour">Portsmouth Harbour</a> are dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Spinnaker_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Spinnaker Tower">Spinnaker Tower</a>, one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_structures_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of tallest structures in the United Kingdom">United Kingdom\'s tallest structures</a> at 560 feet (170&#160;m). Nearby <a href="/wiki/Southsea" title="Southsea">Southsea</a> is a seaside resort with a <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Pier" title="Clarence Pier">pier</a> amusement park and medieval <a href="/wiki/Southsea_Castle" title="Southsea Castle">castle</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth F.C.</a>, the city\'s professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club, play their home games at <a href="/wiki/Fratton_Park" title="Fratton Park">Fratton Park</a>. The city has several mainline railway stations that connect to <a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo" class="mw-redirect" title="London Waterloo">London Waterloo</a> amongst other lines in southern England. <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_International_Port" title="Portsmouth International Port">Portsmouth International Port</a> is a commercial cruise ship and ferry port for international destinations. The port is the second busiest in the United Kingdom after <a href="/wiki/Dover" title="Dover">Dover</a>, handling around three million passengers a year. The city formerly had its own airport, <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Airport_(Hampshire)" title="Portsmouth Airport (Hampshire)">Portsmouth Airport</a>, until its closure in 1973. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Portsmouth" title="University of Portsmouth">University of Portsmouth</a> enrols 23,000 students and is ranked among the world\'s best modern universities. Portsmouth is also the birthplace of author <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a> and engineer <a href="/wiki/Isambard_Kingdom_Brunel" title="Isambard Kingdom Brunel">Isambard Kingdom Brunel</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Literature"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Literature</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Landmarks"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Landmarks</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Gunwharf_Quays"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Gunwharf Quays</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Southsea"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Southsea</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Transport_and_communications"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Transport and communications</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Ferries"><span class="tocnumber">13.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ferries</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Buses"><span class="tocnumber">13.2</span> <span class="toctext">Buses</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Railways"><span class="tocnumber">13.3</span> <span class="toctext">Railways</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Airport"><span class="tocnumber">13.4</span> <span class="toctext">Airport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Possible_public_transport_projects"><span class="tocnumber">13.5</span> <span class="toctext">Possible public transport projects</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Media"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Notable_residents"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Notable residents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">18.1</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">19</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portsmouth" title="History of Portsmouth">History of Portsmouth</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Romans</a> built <a href="/wiki/Portus_Adurni" title="Portus Adurni">Portus Adurni</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Castra" title="Castra">fort</a>, at nearby <a href="/wiki/Portchester" title="Portchester">Portchester</a> in the late third century.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> name "Portesmu\xc3\xb0a" is derived from <i>port</i>, meaning a haven, and <i>mu\xc3\xb0a</i>, the mouth of a large river or estuary.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_Chronicle" title="Anglo-Saxon Chronicle">Anglo-Saxon Chronicle</a></i> has a warrior called Port and his two sons killing a noble Briton in Portsmouth in 501.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, in his <i><a href="/wiki/A_History_of_the_English-Speaking_Peoples" title="A History of the English-Speaking Peoples">A History of the English-Speaking Peoples</a></i>, says that Port was a pirate and he founded Portsmouth in 501.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The south coast was vulnerable to <a href="/wiki/Danes_(Germanic_tribe)" title="Danes (Germanic tribe)">Danish Viking</a> invasions during the 8th and 9th centuries. In 787, it was assaulted and conquered by Danish pirates,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201526_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201526-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and then during the reign of <a href="/wiki/%C3%86thelwulf" title="\xc3\x86thelwulf">\xc3\x86thelwulf</a>, King of <a href="/wiki/Wessex" title="Wessex">Wessex</a> in 838, a Danish fleet landed between Portsmouth and Southampton and the surrounding area was plundered.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201527_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201527-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In response, \xc3\x86thelwulf sent Wulfherd and the governor of <a href="/wiki/Dorsetshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Dorsetshire">Dorsetshire</a> to confront the Danes at Portsmouth, where most of their ships were docked. They were successful although Wulfherd was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201527_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201527-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 1001, the Danes returned and pillaged Portsmouth and surrounding locations, threatening the English with extinction.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201529_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201529-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201530_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201530-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The Danes were massacred by the survivors the following year and rebuilding began, although the town suffered further attacks until 1066.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201531_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201531-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norman_to_Tudor">Norman to Tudor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Norman to Tudor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Round_Tower_(Portsmouth)2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A front facing view of Portsmouth&#39;s Round Tower, which once guarded the entrance to Portsmouth Harbour. The Round Tower itself is made of stone and has a large circular base." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Round_Tower_%28Portsmouth%292009.jpg/220px-Round_Tower_%28Portsmouth%292009.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Round_Tower_%28Portsmouth%292009.jpg/330px-Round_Tower_%28Portsmouth%292009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Round_Tower_%28Portsmouth%292009.jpg/440px-Round_Tower_%28Portsmouth%292009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3879" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Round_Tower_(Portsmouth)2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Round_Tower_(Portsmouth)" title="Round Tower (Portsmouth)">Round Tower</a> was built in 1418 to defend the entrance to <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Harbour" title="Portsmouth Harbour">Portsmouth Harbour</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Portsmouth was not mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/Domesday_Survey" class="mw-redirect" title="Domesday Survey">Domesday Survey</a> of 1086, but <i>Bocheland</i> (<a href="/wiki/Buckland,_Portsmouth" title="Buckland, Portsmouth">Buckland</a>), <i>Copenore</i> (<a href="/wiki/Copnor" title="Copnor">Copnor</a>), and <i>Frodentone</i> (<a href="/wiki/Fratton" title="Fratton">Fratton</a>) were.<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Some sources maintain it was founded in 1180 by the Anglo-Norman merchant <a href="/wiki/Jean_de_Gisors" title="Jean de Gisors">Jean de Gisors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When King <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_England" title="Henry II of England">Henry II</a> died in 1189, his son <a href="/wiki/Richard_I_of_England" title="Richard I of England">Richard I</a>, who had spent most of his life in France, arrived in Portsmouth before he was crowned in London.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201532_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201532-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> When Richard returned from captivity in <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Austria" title="Duchy of Austria">Austria</a> in May 1194, he summoned a fleet of 100 ships and an army to the port.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201533_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201533-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> He granted the town a <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">royal charter</a> on 2 May, giving permission for an annual fifteen-day free market fair, weekly markets, and a local court to deal with minor matters, and exempted its inhabitants from paying an annual tax of \xc2\xa318.<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuail199414\xe2\x80\x9318_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuail199414\xe2\x80\x9318-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Richard granted the town the arms of <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Komnenos_of_Cyprus" title="Isaac Komnenos of Cyprus">Isaac Komnenos of Cyprus</a>, whom he had defeated during the <a href="/wiki/Third_Crusade" title="Third Crusade">Third Crusade</a> in 1191, reflecting a significant involvement of local soldiers, sailors, and vessels in the holy war.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The 800 anniversary was celebrated in 1994 as the city\'s founding<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/John,_King_of_England" title="John, King of England">King John</a> reaffirmed the rights and privileges awarded by Richard<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>I and established the permanent naval base. The first docks were built by <a href="/wiki/William_of_Wrotham" title="William of Wrotham">William of Wrotham</a> beginning in 1212.<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201533_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201533-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> John summoned his earls, barons, and military advisers to the town to plan an invasion of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Normandy" title="Duchy of Normandy">Normandy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201534_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201534-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In 1229, after a declaration of war against France, <a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_England" title="Henry III of England">Henry<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>III</a> assembled a force described as "one of the finest armies that had ever been raised in England" by historian Lake Allen.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201536_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201536-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The invasion stalled and returned from France in October 1231.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201537_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201537-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In 1242 Henry<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>III summoned troops to invade <a href="/wiki/Guienne" class="mw-redirect" title="Guienne">Guienne</a>, and in 1295 <a href="/wiki/Edward_I_of_England" title="Edward I of England">Edward<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>I</a> sent supplies for his army in France.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201537,_39_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201537,_39-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> By the following century, commercial interests had grown and its exports included wool, corn, grain, and livestock.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201543_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201543-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Edward_II_of_England" title="Edward II of England">Edward II</a> ordered all ports on the south coast to assemble their largest vessels at Portsmouth to carry soldiers and horses to the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Aquitaine" title="Duchy of Aquitaine">Duchy of Aquitaine</a> in 1324 to strengthen defences.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201544_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201544-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In 1336 a French fleet under the command of <a href="/wiki/David_II_of_Scotland" title="David II of Scotland">David II of Scotland</a> attacked the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a>, ransacked the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a> and threatened the town. Concerned, <a href="/wiki/Edward_III_of_England" title="Edward III of England">Edward<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>III</a> instructed all maritime towns to build vessels and raise troops to rendezvous at Portsmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201544_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201544-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Two years later, a French fleet led by <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_B%C3%A9huchet" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicholas B\xc3\xa9huchet">Nicholas B\xc3\xa9huchet</a> <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_Portsmouth_(1338)" class="mw-redirect" title="Raid on Portsmouth (1338)">raided Portsmouth</a>, destroying much of the town. Only the stone-built church and hospital survived.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESumption1990395,_396_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESumption1990395,_396-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESeward1988_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESeward1988-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> After the raid, Edward<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>III exempted the town from national taxes to aid reconstruction.<sup id="cite_ref-porthis_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-porthis-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Upon Edward<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>III\'s death in 1377, his grandson <a href="/wiki/Richard_II_of_England" title="Richard II of England">Richard<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>II</a> was crowned, and the French landed in Portsmouth in the same year. The town was plundered and burnt, but its inhabitants fought back and defeated them, which led the French to retreat and raid towns in the <a href="/wiki/West_Country" title="West Country">West Country</a> instead.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201548_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201548-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_portsmouth_a_bit_before_1540.PNG" class="image"><img alt="A black and white map of Portsmouth dated around 1540." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Map_of_portsmouth_a_bit_before_1540.PNG/220px-Map_of_portsmouth_a_bit_before_1540.PNG" width="220" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Map_of_portsmouth_a_bit_before_1540.PNG/330px-Map_of_portsmouth_a_bit_before_1540.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Map_of_portsmouth_a_bit_before_1540.PNG/440px-Map_of_portsmouth_a_bit_before_1540.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1928" data-file-height="1860" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_portsmouth_a_bit_before_1540.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of Portsmouth in around 1540.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Henry_V_of_England" title="Henry V of England">Henry V</a> built the first permanent <a href="/wiki/Fortifications_of_Portsmouth" title="Fortifications of Portsmouth">fortifications of Portsmouth</a>. In 1416, a number of French ships blockaded Portsmouth, which housed ships that were set to invade Normandy. Instead, Henry gathered a fleet at Southampton and invaded the Norman coast in August of that year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201549_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201549-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Recognising the town\'s growing importance, he ordered a wooden <a href="/wiki/Round_Tower_(Portsmouth)" title="Round Tower (Portsmouth)">Round Tower</a> to be built at the mouth of the harbour, which was completed in 1426.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201327_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201327-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII</a> rebuilt the fortifications with stone, assisted Robert Brygandine and Sir <a href="/wiki/Reginald_Bray" title="Reginald Bray">Reginald Bray</a> in the construction of the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Dry_dock" title="Dry dock">dry dock</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201333_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201333-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> and raised the <a href="/wiki/Square_Tower" title="Square Tower">Square Tower</a> in 1494.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201327_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201327-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> During his reign, Henry<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>VII made Portsmouth a Royal Dock, and was England\'s only dockyard to be considered "national" at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201553_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201553-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Alfred_the_Great" title="Alfred the Great">King Alfred</a> may have used Portsmouth to build ships as early as the 9th century, the first warship recorded as constructed in the town was the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sweepstake_(warship)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sweepstake (warship) (page does not exist)"><i>Sweepstake</i></a>, built in the dry dock in 1497.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1539, <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII</a> built <a href="/wiki/Southsea_Castle" title="Southsea Castle">Southsea Castle</a>, financed by the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Monasteries" title="Dissolution of the Monasteries">Dissolution of the Monasteries</a>, in anticipation of a French invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen2015143_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen2015143-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> He also invested large sums of money into the town\'s dockyard, and expanded its boundaries to 8 acres (3.2&#160;ha).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201323_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201323-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Around this time a Tudor <a href="/wiki/Boom_(navigational_barrier)" title="Boom (navigational barrier)">defensive boom</a> stretched from the Round Tower to Fort Blockhouse in Gosport, as a protection to Portsmouth Harbour.<sup id="cite_ref-boom_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boom-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>In 1545, from Southsea Castle, he witnessed his flagship <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_Rose" title="Mary Rose">Mary Rose</a></i> sink with the loss of about 500 lives, whilst going into action against the French fleet in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Solent" title="Battle of the Solent">Battle of the Solent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Some historians believe that the <i>Mary Rose</i> turned too quickly and submerged her open gun ports, whereas others argue that it sank due to its poor design.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201337_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201337-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Over the years, Portsmouth\'s fortifications were rebuilt and improved by successive monarchs. In 1563, Portsmouth suffered from an outbreak of a <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">plague</a>, resulting in about 300 deaths out of the town\'s population of 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stuart_to_Georgian">Stuart to Georgian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Stuart to Georgian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Portsmouth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A view of Old Portsmouth taken from the viewing deck of the Spinnaker Tower. Old buildings, cobbled streets and a small island can be seen in the frame." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Old_Portsmouth.jpg/220px-Old_Portsmouth.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Old_Portsmouth.jpg/330px-Old_Portsmouth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Old_Portsmouth.jpg/440px-Old_Portsmouth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2649" data-file-height="1717" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Portsmouth.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of <a href="/wiki/Old_Portsmouth" title="Old Portsmouth">Old Portsmouth</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Spinnaker_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Spinnaker Tower">Spinnaker Tower</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1623, <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I</a> (then Prince of Wales) returned to Portsmouth from his travels in France and Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201554_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201554-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Five years later, Charles\' unpopular military adviser, <a href="/wiki/George_Villiers,_1st_Duke_of_Buckingham" title="George Villiers, 1st Duke of Buckingham">George Villiers, 1st Duke of Buckingham</a>, was stabbed to death in an <a href="/wiki/Old_Portsmouth" title="Old Portsmouth">Old Portsmouth</a> pub by war veteran <a href="/wiki/John_Felton_(assassin)" title="John Felton (assassin)">John Felton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201554,_55_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201554,_55-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Felton never attempted to escape and was caught walking through the streets when soldiers confronted him, to which he responded: "I know that he is dead, for I had the force of forty men when I struck the blow".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201556_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201556-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Felton was then hanged, and his body was chained to a <a href="/wiki/Gibbet" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibbet">gibbet</a> on <a href="/wiki/Southsea_Common" class="mw-redirect" title="Southsea Common">Southsea Common</a> as a warning to others.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201556_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201556-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The murder took place in the Greyhound public house on High Street, which is now private and called Buckingham House; it bears a commemorative plaque.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most residents, including the mayor, supported the <a href="/wiki/Roundhead" title="Roundhead">parliamentarians</a> during the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>, although its military governor, <a href="/wiki/George_Goring,_Lord_Goring" title="George Goring, Lord Goring">Colonel Goring</a>, supported the <a href="/wiki/Cavalier" title="Cavalier">royalists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The town became a major base for the parliamentarian navy and was blockaded from the sea. Parliamentarian troops were sent to raid it by land in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Portsmouth" title="Siege of Portsmouth">Siege of Portsmouth</a>; the guns of Southsea Castle were fired at the royalist garrison in the town. Across the harbour, parliamentarians in <a href="/wiki/Gosport" title="Gosport">Gosport</a> joined in the assault, with their guns damaging <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Cathedral" title="Portsmouth Cathedral">St Thomas\'s Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-siege_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-siege-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On 5 September 1642, the remaining royalists in the garrison at the Square Tower were forced to surrender after Goring threatened to blow it up with gunpowder. In return, he and his garrison were allowed safe passage.<sup id="cite_ref-siege_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-siege-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-siege1_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-siege1-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_England" title="Commonwealth of England">Commonwealth of England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Blake_(admiral)" title="Robert Blake (admiral)">Robert Blake</a> used the harbour as his base during the <a href="/wiki/First_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="First Anglo-Dutch War">First Anglo-Dutch War</a> in 1652 and the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1654%E2%80%9360)" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1654\xe2\x80\x9360)">Anglo Spanish War</a> of 1654. He died within sight of the town returning from <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="C\xc3\xa1diz">C\xc3\xa1diz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-siege1_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-siege1-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> After the end of the Civil War in 1646, Portsmouth was among the first towns to declare <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>II</a> as king and subsequently began to prosper.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201557_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201557-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In 1650, the first ship to be built for more than 100 years, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Portsmouth_(1650)" title="HMS Portsmouth (1650)">HMS&#160;<i>Portsmouth</i></a>, was launched. Between 1650 and 1660, twelve ships were built. After the <a href="/wiki/Restoration_(England)" title="Restoration (England)">restoration of Monarchy</a>, Charles<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>II married <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Braganza" title="Catherine of Braganza">Catherine of Braganza</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Domus_Dei" title="Domus Dei">Royal Garrison Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-garr_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-garr-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201357_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201357-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> During the latter half of the 17th century the town continued to grow; a new wharf was constructed in 1663 for military use, and in 1665 a <a href="/wiki/Mast_(sailing)" title="Mast (sailing)">mast</a> pond was dug out. In 1684 a list of ships docked in Portsmouth gave evidence of its increasing national importance; the town was the only place of naval rendezvous in England at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201558_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201558-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Between 1667 and 1685 the town\'s fortifications were rebuilt; new walls were constructed with <a href="/wiki/Bastion" title="Bastion">bastions</a> and two moats were dug, making Portsmouth one of the most heavily fortified places in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1759, General <a href="/wiki/James_Wolfe" title="James Wolfe">James Wolfe</a> sailed from the harbour to Canada on an expedition to capture <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> which, though successful, cost him his life. His body was brought back to Portsmouth in November that year and received the highest naval and military honours.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen201565_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen201565-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Two years later, on 30 May 1775, Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> arrived on board <a href="/wiki/HMS_Endeavour" title="HMS Endeavour">HMS&#160;<i>Endeavour</i></a> after circumnavigating the world.<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollingridge2003311_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollingridge2003311-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On 13 May 1787, <a href="/wiki/First_Fleet" title="First Fleet">eleven ships left</a> to establish the first European colony in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, marking the beginning of prisoner transportation,<sup id="cite_ref-Gutenberg_FF_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gutenberg_FF-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrost2012165_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrost2012165-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> and in the same year, Captain <a href="/wiki/William_Bligh" title="William Bligh">William Bligh</a> of <a href="/wiki/HMS_Bounty" title="HMS Bounty">HMS&#160;<i>Bounty</i></a> set sail from the harbour.<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013223_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013223-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Mutiny_on_the_Bounty" title="Mutiny on the Bounty">mutiny on the <i>Bounty</i></a> on 28 April 1789, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Pandora_(1779)" title="HMS Pandora (1779)">HMS&#160;<i>Pandora</i></a> was dispatched from Portsmouth to bring back the mutineers for trial. The court martial opened on 12 September 1792 on board <a href="/wiki/HMS_Duke_(1777)" title="HMS Duke (1777)">HMS&#160;<i>Duke</i></a> in Portsmouth Harbour&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 of the remaining ten men, three were sentenced to death.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013223,_224_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013223,_224-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHough1972276_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHough1972276-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> In 1789, a chapel was erected in Prince George\'s Street and was dedicated to <a href="/wiki/John_the_Apostle" title="John the Apostle">St John</a> by the Bishop of Winchester. Around this time, a <a href="/wiki/Bill_(law)" title="Bill (law)">bill</a> was passed in the House of Commons regarding the creation of a canal to link Portsmouth to Chichester, but the project was abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen2015130_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen2015130-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city\'s nickname Pompey is thought to have derived from the log entry of <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Point" title="Portsmouth Point">Portsmouth Point</a>, contracted to "Po\'m.P." (<b>Po\'</b>rts<b>m</b>outh <b>P.</b>oint) as ships entered the harbour. Navigational charts use the contraction.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> However, a historian argues that the name Pompey may have been brought back from a group of Portsmouth-based sailors who visited <a href="/wiki/Pompey%27s_Pillar_(column)" title="Pompey&#39;s Pillar (column)">Pompey\'s Pillar</a> in <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>, Egypt, in around 1781.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201398_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201398-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Another theory is that it is named after the harbour\'s guardship, <i><a href="/wiki/French_ship_Pomp%C3%A9e_(1793)" class="mw-redirect" title="French ship Pomp\xc3\xa9e (1793)">Pompee</a></i>, a 74-gun French ship of the line captured in 1793.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBreverton2010282_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBreverton2010282-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The borough\'s coat of arms is attested in the early 19th century, as <i>Azure a crescent or, surmounted by an estoile of eight points of the last</i><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\nThis design is apparently based on seals of the mayoralty used in the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_Revolution_to_Victorian">Industrial Revolution to Victorian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Industrial Revolution to Victorian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warrior_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A picture of the iron-clad HMS Warrior docked in Portsmouth&#39;s historic harbour. The ship has since been restored to its original Victorian condition." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Warrior_1.JPG/220px-Warrior_1.JPG" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Warrior_1.JPG/330px-Warrior_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Warrior_1.JPG/440px-Warrior_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2368" data-file-height="1732" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warrior_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMS_Warrior_(1860)" title="HMS Warrior (1860)">HMS&#160;<i>Warrior</i></a> (launched in 1860) has been restored to its original Victorian condition.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Marc_Isambard_Brunel" title="Marc Isambard Brunel">Marc Isambard Brunel</a> established the world\'s first mass production line at <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Block_Mills" title="Portsmouth Block Mills">Portsmouth Block Mills</a> making <a href="/wiki/Pulley" title="Pulley">pulley</a> <a href="/wiki/Block_(sailing)" title="Block (sailing)">blocks</a> for <a href="/wiki/Rigging" title="Rigging">rigging</a> on the navy\'s ships.<sup id="cite_ref-royal_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-royal-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The first machines were installed in January 1803 and the final set for large blocks in March 1805. In 1808, the mills produced 130,000 blocks.<sup id="cite_ref-block_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-block-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> By the turn of the 19th century, the town had the largest industrial site in the world with a workforce of 8000 and an annual budget of \xc2\xa3570,000.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1805, <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Nelson" class="mw-redirect" title="Horatio Nelson">Admiral Nelson</a> left Portsmouth to command the fleet that defeated the Franco-Spanish at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Battle of Trafalgar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Before departing, Nelson told the crew of <a href="/wiki/HMS_Victory" title="HMS Victory">HMS&#160;<i>Victory</i></a> and workers in the dockyard that "England expects every man will do his duty".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201339_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201339-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The Royal Navy\'s reliance on Portsmouth led to it becoming the most fortified city in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPevsner1967422_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPevsner1967422-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> A network of <a href="/wiki/Palmerston_Forts,_Portsmouth" title="Palmerston Forts, Portsmouth">Palmerston Forts</a> were built around the town as part of a programme led by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Lord_Palmerston" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Palmerston">Lord Palmerston</a> to defend British military bases from an inland attack. The forts were nicknamed "Palmerston\'s Follies" due to the fact that their armaments were pointed inland and not out to sea.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201379_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201379-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> From 1808 the Royal Navy\'s <a href="/wiki/West_Africa_Squadron" title="West Africa Squadron">West Africa Squadron</a>, tasked with stopping the slave trade, operated out of Portsmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_slave_trade_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_slave_trade-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 1811 the Portsea Island Company constructed the first piped water supply<sup id="cite_ref-water_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-water-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> to upper and middle class houses.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> It supplied water to approximately 4500 of the 14,000 houses, generating an income \xc2\xa35000 a year.<sup id="cite_ref-water_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-water-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> HMS <i>Victory</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s active career ended in 1812, when she was moored in Portsmouth Harbour and used as a <a href="/wiki/Depot_ship" title="Depot ship">depot ship</a>. The town of Gosport contributed \xc2\xa375 a year towards the ship\'s maintenance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201339_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201339-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In 1818, <a href="/wiki/John_Pounds" title="John Pounds">John Pounds</a> began teaching working class children in the country\'s first <a href="/wiki/Ragged_school" title="Ragged school">ragged school</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201366,_67_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201366,_67-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In 1820, the Portsea Improvement Commissioners installed gas street lighting throughout the town,<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> followed by Old Portsmouth three years later.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 19th century, Portsmouth grew and expanded across Portsea Island. By the 1860s <a href="/wiki/Buckland,_Portsmouth" title="Buckland, Portsmouth">Buckland</a> had been merged into the expanding town, and by the next decade <a href="/wiki/Fratton" title="Fratton">Fratton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stamshaw" title="Stamshaw">Stamshaw</a> had also been incorporated. Between 1865 and 1870 the council built sewers after more than 800 people died in a <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> epidemic. A bylaw stated that any house within 100 feet (30&#160;m) of a sewer had to be connected to it.<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> By 1871 the population had risen to 100,000,<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> although the national census at that time gave the population as 113,569.<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> A working-class suburb was constructed in the 1870s when around 1,820 houses were built on land owned by a Mr<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Somers. The suburb became <a href="/wiki/Somerstown,_Hampshire" title="Somerstown, Hampshire">Somerstown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Despite public health improvements, 514 people died in a <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> epidemic in 1872.<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> That year, on 21 December, the <a href="/wiki/Challenger_expedition" title="Challenger expedition"><i>Challenger</i> expedition</a> was launched from Portsmouth, embarking on a 68,890-nautical-mile (127,580&#160;km) circumnavigation of the globe for scientific research.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERice199927\xe2\x80\x9348_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERice199927\xe2\x80\x9348-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Edwardian_to_Second_World_War">Edwardian to Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Edwardian to Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:George_VI_inspecting_the_crew_of_HNoMS_Draug.jpg" class="image"><img alt="In this photograph, King George VI is inspecting the crew of the Norwegian ship HNoMS Draug, which was docked in Portsmouth sometime during the war." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/George_VI_inspecting_the_crew_of_HNoMS_Draug.jpg/220px-George_VI_inspecting_the_crew_of_HNoMS_Draug.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/33/George_VI_inspecting_the_crew_of_HNoMS_Draug.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="325" data-file-height="218" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:George_VI_inspecting_the_crew_of_HNoMS_Draug.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">George VI</a> inspecting the crew of the <a href="/wiki/HNoMS_Draug_(1908)" title="HNoMS Draug (1908)">HNoMS <i>Draug</i></a> in Portsmouth during the Second World War</div></div></div>\n<p>At the turn of the 20th century, Portsmouth was considered "the world\'s greatest naval port" when the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> was at its height of power, covering a quarter of Earth\'s total land area and 458 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201324_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201324-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In 1900, Portsmouth Dockyard employed 8000 men<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>\xe2\x80\x93 a figure which more than doubled to 23,000 people during the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201391_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201391-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> On 1 October 1916, Portsmouth was bombed by a <a href="/wiki/Zeppelin" title="Zeppelin">Zeppelin</a> airship.<sup id="cite_ref-nazi1_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nazi1-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Although the <i><a href="/wiki/Oberste_Heeresleitung" title="Oberste Heeresleitung">Oberste Heeresleitung</a></i> (German Supreme Army Command) stated that the town was "lavishly bombarded with good results", there were no reports of any bombs being dropped in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Another source asserted that the bombs were mistakenly dropped into the harbour rather than the dockyard.<sup id="cite_ref-nazi1_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nazi1-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Throughout the war, around 1200 ships were refitted in the dockyard, making it one of the most strategic ports in the empire at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201391_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201391-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Portsmouth was granted <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city status</a> in 1926, following a long campaign by the borough council. The application was made on the grounds that it was the "first naval port of the kingdom".<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> In 1929, the city council added the <a href="/wiki/Motto" title="Motto">motto</a> "Heaven\'s Light Our Guide" to the medieval coat of arms. Except for the celestial objects in the arms, the motto was that of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Star_of_India" title="Order of the Star of India">Star of India</a>, referring to the troopships bound for <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British India</a> that left from the port.<sup id="cite_ref-blu_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blu-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The crest and supporters are based on those of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_arms_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal arms of the United Kingdom">royal arms</a>, but altered to show the city\'s maritime connections: the lions and unicorn have been given fish tails, and a <a href="/wiki/Naval_crown" title="Naval crown">naval crown</a> placed around the unicorn.<sup id="cite_ref-blu_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blu-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Around the unicorn is wrapped a representation of the Tudor defensive boom which stretched across Portsmouth Harbour.<sup id="cite_ref-boom_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boom-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, the city, particularly the port, was bombed extensively by the <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Blitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Portsmouth Blitz">Portsmouth Blitz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history3_21-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history3-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\nBetween July 1940 and May 1944, the city was hit by 67 air raids which destroyed 6625 houses and severely damaged 6549 of them.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The air raids caused 930 deaths and wounded almost 3000 people,<sup id="cite_ref-guild_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guild-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> many of them in the dockyard and military establishments.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> On the night of the city\'s heaviest raid on 10 January 1941, the Luftwaffe dropped 140 tonnes of high explosive bombs, killing 171 people and leaving 3000 homeless.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013151_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013151-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Many of the city\'s houses were damaged and areas of <a href="/wiki/Landport" title="Landport">Landport</a> and Old Portsmouth destroyed, with the future site of <a href="/wiki/Gunwharf_Quays" title="Gunwharf Quays">Gunwharf Quays</a> being razed to the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013186_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013186-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> On the same night, the <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Guildhall" title="Portsmouth Guildhall">Guildhall</a> was hit by an incendiary bomb which burnt out the interior and destroyed its inner walls,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013147_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013147-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> although the civic plate was retrieved unharmed from the vault under the front steps.<sup id="cite_ref-guild_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guild-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Following the heaviest raid on the city, Portsmouth\'s mayor, Sir Denis Daley, wrote in the <i>Evening News</i>:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We are bruised but we are not daunted, and we are still as determined as ever to stand side by side with other cities who have felt the blast of the enemy, and we shall, with them, persevere with an unflagging spirit towards a conclusive and decisive victory.</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite>Sir Denis Daley, January 1941<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013146_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013146-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>Portsmouth Harbour was a vital military embarkation point for the <a href="/wiki/D-Day_landings" class="mw-redirect" title="D-Day landings">D-Day landings</a> on 6 June 1944. <a href="/wiki/Southwick_House" title="Southwick House">Southwick House</a>, just to the north of the city, was the headquarters of the Supreme Allied Commander, US General <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013155,_156_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013155,_156-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> On 15 July 1944 a <a href="/wiki/V-1_flying_bomb" title="V-1 flying bomb">V-1 flying bomb</a> hit Newcomen Road, killing 15 people.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war">Post-war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Post-war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Much of the city\'s housing stock was damaged during the war. The wreckage was cleared in an attempt to improve the quality of dwellings after the war, though before permanent accommodation could be built, Portsmouth City Council built <a href="/wiki/Prefabs_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prefabs in the United Kingdom">prefabs</a> for those who had lost their homes. Between 1945 and 1947, more than 700 prefab houses were constructed<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>\xe2\x80\x93 some were erected over bomb sites.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The first permanent houses were built away from the city centre to new developments such as <a href="/wiki/Paulsgrove" title="Paulsgrove">Paulsgrove</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leigh_Park" title="Leigh Park">Leigh Park</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013160_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013160-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Leigh_Park_history_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leigh_Park_history-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> with construction of council estates in Paulsgrove being completed in 1953. In Leigh Park, the first housing estates were completed in 1949, though building work in the area continued until 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Developers still occasionally find <a href="/wiki/Unexploded_ordnance" title="Unexploded ordnance">unexploded bombs</a> in the area, such as on the site of the destroyed Hippodrome theatre in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Despite improvements made by the city council to build new accommodation, a survey made in 1955 concluded that 7000 houses in Portsmouth were unfit for human habitation. Following a controversial decision, a whole section of central Portsmouth, including Landport, Somerstown and Buckland, was demolished and replaced by council housing during the 1960s and early 1970s. The success of the project and the quality of the 70s homes are debatable.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Royal_Yacht_Britannia_in_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1702549.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Her Majesty&#39;s Yacht Britannia is docked in Portsmouth Harbour for the 50th anniversary of the D-Day Landings in 1994. More modern Royal Navy ships are docked in behind her, and the masts of the HMS Victory can be seen in the far background." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/The_Royal_Yacht_Britannia_in_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1702549.jpg/220px-The_Royal_Yacht_Britannia_in_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1702549.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/The_Royal_Yacht_Britannia_in_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1702549.jpg/330px-The_Royal_Yacht_Britannia_in_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1702549.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/The_Royal_Yacht_Britannia_in_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1702549.jpg/440px-The_Royal_Yacht_Britannia_in_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1702549.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="969" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Royal_Yacht_Britannia_in_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1702549.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMY_Britannia" title="HMY Britannia">Her Majesty\'s Yacht <i>Britannia</i></a> in Portsmouth Harbour during the 50th anniversary of the D-Day Landings in 1994. The masts of <a href="/wiki/HMS_Victory" title="HMS Victory">HMS&#160;<i>Victory</i></a> can be seen in the background.</div></div></div>\n<p>Portsmouth was affected by the British Empire\'s decline in the latter half of the 20th century. Shipbuilding jobs fell from 46% of workforce in 1951 to 14% in 1966, drastically reducing the manpower in the dockyard. The city council attempted to create new work; an industrial estate was built in Fratton in 1948, and others were built at Paulsgrove and Farlington in the 1950s and 1960s, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Traditional industries such as brewing and corset making disappeared during this time, though electrical engineering became a major employer. Despite the cutbacks made to traditional sectors, Portsmouth still remained an attractive place for industry. In 1968, <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Insurance_Group" title="Zurich Insurance Group">Zurich Insurance Group</a> moved their UK headquarters to the city, with <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> relocating their European headquarters in 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The population of the city had dropped from approximately 200,000 to 177,142 by the end of the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013161_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013161-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> In the early 1980s, then Defence Secretary <a href="/wiki/John_Nott" title="John Nott">John Nott</a> concluded that of the four home dockyards, both Portsmouth and <a href="/wiki/Chatham_Dockyard" title="Chatham Dockyard">Chatham</a> would be closed. However, Portsmouth City Council won a concession, and rather than face closure, the dockyard was downgraded to a naval base.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201392_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201392-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 2 April 1982, Argentine forces invaded two British territories in the South Atlantic: the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands</a>. The British government\'s response was to dispatch a <a href="/wiki/British_logistics_in_the_Falklands_War" title="British logistics in the Falklands War">naval task force</a>, and on 5 April, the aircraft carriers <a href="/wiki/HMS_Hermes_(R12)" title="HMS Hermes (R12)">HMS&#160;<i>Hermes</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Invincible_(R05)" title="HMS Invincible (R05)">HMS&#160;<i>Invincible</i></a> sailed from Portsmouth for the South Atlantic. The successful outcome of the war had reaffirmed Portsmouth\'s significance as a naval port and importance to the defence of British interests.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201393_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201393-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> In January 1997, <a href="/wiki/HMY_Britannia" title="HMY Britannia">Her Majesty\'s Yacht <i>Britannia</i></a> embarked from the city on her final voyage to oversee the <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_sovereignty_over_Hong_Kong" class="mw-redirect" title="Transfer of sovereignty over Hong Kong">transfer of sovereignty over Hong Kong</a>, which marked for many the end of the empire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrendon2007660_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrendon2007660-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> She was later decommissioned on 11 December that year at Portsmouth Naval Base in the presence of the Queen, the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Duke of Edinburgh">Duke of Edinburgh</a>, and twelve senior members of the Royal Family.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2001, redevelopment of the <a href="/wiki/HMS_Vernon_(shore_establishment)" title="HMS Vernon (shore establishment)">naval shore establishment HMS <i>Vernon</i></a> began as a complex of retail outlets, clubs, pubs, and a large shopping centre known as Gunwharf Quays.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, construction of the 552 feet (168&#160;m) tall <a href="/wiki/Spinnaker_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Spinnaker Tower">Spinnaker Tower</a> began at Gunwharf Quays with sponsorship from the <a href="/wiki/National_Lottery_(United_Kingdom)" title="National Lottery (United Kingdom)">National Lottery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> In late 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Tricorn_Centre" title="Tricorn Centre">Tricorn Centre</a>, dubbed "the ugliest building in the UK" by the BBC, was demolished after years of debate over the expense of demolition, and controversy as to whether it was worth preserving as an example of 1960s <a href="/wiki/Brutalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Brutalist">brutalist</a> <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClark2009_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark2009-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> It was designed by <a href="/wiki/Owen_Luder" title="Owen Luder">Owen Luder</a> as part of a project to "revitalise" Portsmouth in the 1960s, consisting of a shopping centre, market, nightclubs, and a <a href="/wiki/Multi-storey_car_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-storey car park">multi-storey car park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013164_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013164-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> In 2005 the city celebrated the 200th anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Battle of Trafalgar</a>, with Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> being present at a formal <a href="/wiki/Fleet_review_(Commonwealth_realms)" title="Fleet review (Commonwealth realms)">fleet review</a> and a staged mock battle.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The naval base continues to be home to two-thirds of the surface fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-RN1_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RN1-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_photograph_of_Portsmouth_Dockyard_taken_during_a_Photex,_taken_from_2,000_feet._MOD_45144955.jpg" class="image"><img alt="An aerial view of western side of Portsmouth (including Gunwharf Quays, the dockyard and the Spinnaker tower), the harbour itself, and the town of Gosport." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Aerial_photograph_of_Portsmouth_Dockyard_taken_during_a_Photex%2C_taken_from_2%2C000_feet._MOD_45144955.jpg/300px-Aerial_photograph_of_Portsmouth_Dockyard_taken_during_a_Photex%2C_taken_from_2%2C000_feet._MOD_45144955.jpg" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Aerial_photograph_of_Portsmouth_Dockyard_taken_during_a_Photex%2C_taken_from_2%2C000_feet._MOD_45144955.jpg/450px-Aerial_photograph_of_Portsmouth_Dockyard_taken_during_a_Photex%2C_taken_from_2%2C000_feet._MOD_45144955.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Aerial_photograph_of_Portsmouth_Dockyard_taken_during_a_Photex%2C_taken_from_2%2C000_feet._MOD_45144955.jpg/600px-Aerial_photograph_of_Portsmouth_Dockyard_taken_during_a_Photex%2C_taken_from_2%2C000_feet._MOD_45144955.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_photograph_of_Portsmouth_Dockyard_taken_during_a_Photex,_taken_from_2,000_feet._MOD_45144955.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of Portsmouth and Portsmouth Harbour</div></div></div>\n<p>By road, Portsmouth lies 73.5 miles (118.3&#160;km) from Central London, 49.5 miles (79.7&#160;km) west of <a href="/wiki/Brighton" title="Brighton">Brighton</a>, and 22.3 miles (35.9&#160;km) east of <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\nPortsmouth is situated primarily on <a href="/wiki/Portsea_Island" title="Portsea Island">Portsea Island</a> and is the United Kingdom\'s only island city, although parts of it have expanded onto the mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201314,_16_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201314,_16-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gosport" title="Gosport">Gosport</a> forms a borough in its own right immediately to the west.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The island is separated from the mainland by <a href="/wiki/Portsbridge_Creek" title="Portsbridge Creek">Portsbridge Creek</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVine1990_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVine1990-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> which is crossed by three road bridges (the <a href="/wiki/M275_motorway" title="M275 motorway">M275 motorway</a>, the <a href="/wiki/A3_road" title="A3 road">A3 road</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/A2030_road" title="A2030 road">A2030 road</a>), a railway bridge, and two footbridges.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> \nPortsea Island, which forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Hampshire_Basin" title="Hampshire Basin">Hampshire Basin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> is low-lying: the majority of its surface area on the island is less than 3 metres (9.8&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rising_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rising-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The highest natural elevation on Portsea Island is the road junction Kingston Cross, at 21 feet (6.4&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-rising_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rising-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Old_Portsmouth" title="Old Portsmouth">Old Portsmouth</a> forms the oldest part of the city in the south-west part of Portsea Island, and includes <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Point" title="Portsmouth Point">Portsmouth Point</a>, historically nicknamed as Spice Island.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The main channel entering Portsmouth Harbour, which lies to the west of Portsea Island,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVine1990_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVine1990-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> passes between Old Portsmouth and Gosport.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Within Portsmouth Harbour are a series of lakes, including Fountain Lake near the harbour, Portchester Lake in the central south, Brick Kiln Lake and Tipner to the east, and Bombketch and Spider Lakes to the west. In the channel further to the northwest, around Portchester, are Wicor, Cams, and Great Cams Lakes.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_114-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> \nThe large tidal inlet of <a href="/wiki/Langstone_Harbour" title="Langstone Harbour">Langstone Harbour</a> lies to the east of Portsea Island. In the northern part, off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Farlington,_Hampshire" title="Farlington, Hampshire">Farlington</a>, is the <a href="/wiki/Farlington_Marshes" title="Farlington Marshes">Farlington Marshes</a>, a 125-hectare (308-acre) grazing marsh and saline lagoon.
