One of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Local_nature_reserve" title="Local nature reserve">local reserves</a> in the county, built from reclaimed land in 1771, it provides an important habitat for migratory wildfowl and <a href="/wiki/Wader" title="Wader">waders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SelseyHaylingPortsea.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A high aerial view of Portsea Island (the island which Portsmouth is situated on), and neighbouring Hayling Island." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/SelseyHaylingPortsea.JPG/170px-SelseyHaylingPortsea.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/SelseyHaylingPortsea.JPG/255px-SelseyHaylingPortsea.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/SelseyHaylingPortsea.JPG/340px-SelseyHaylingPortsea.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3168" data-file-height="4224" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SelseyHaylingPortsea.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portsea Island and Hayling Island</div></div></div>\n<p>To the south of Portsmouth are the waters of <a href="/wiki/Spithead" title="Spithead">Spithead</a>, the wider <a href="/wiki/Solent" title="Solent">Solent</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a>. The southern coast of the city was historically fortified by the <a href="/wiki/Round_Tower_(Portsmouth)" title="Round Tower (Portsmouth)">Round Tower</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Square_Tower" title="Square Tower">Square Tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southsea_Castle" title="Southsea Castle">Southsea Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lumps_Fort" title="Lumps Fort">Lumps Fort</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Cumberland_(England)" title="Fort Cumberland (England)">Fort Cumberland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatterson1985_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatterson1985-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Four sea forts were built in the Solent to protect Portsmouth by <a href="/wiki/Henry_John_Temple,_3rd_Viscount_Palmerston" title="Henry John Temple, 3rd Viscount Palmerston">Lord Palmerston</a>, these are named <a href="/wiki/Spitbank_Fort" title="Spitbank Fort">Spitbank Fort</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_Fort" title="St Helens Fort">St Helens Fort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horse_Sand_Fort" title="Horse Sand Fort">Horse Sand Fort</a> and <a href="/wiki/No_Mans_Land_Fort" class="mw-redirect" title="No Mans Land Fort">No Mans Land Fort</a>.\n</p><p>The seaside resort of <a href="/wiki/Southsea" title="Southsea">Southsea</a> is situated to the south of Portsea Island,<sup id="cite_ref-pissea_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pissea-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> and to the east lies the area known as <a href="/wiki/Eastney" title="Eastney">Eastney</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eastney_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eastney-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Eastney Lake covered nearly 170 acres (69 hectares) in 1626.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWebb198911_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWebb198911-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> To the north of Eastney is the residential district of <a href="/wiki/Milton,_Portsmouth" title="Milton, Portsmouth">Milton</a> and an area of reclaimed land now known as Milton Common (formerly Milton Lake),<sup id="cite_ref-GM_114-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> described as a "flat scrubby land with a series of freshwater lakes".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELong2007188_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELong2007188-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Further north on the east coast is the residential district of <a href="/wiki/Baffins" title="Baffins">Baffins</a>, featuring Great Salterns recreation ground and golf course, which forms an area around <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_College" title="Portsmouth College">Portsmouth College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_114-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Hilsea_Lines" title="Hilsea Lines">Hilsea Lines</a> are a series of defunct fortifications on the north coast of the island which border Portsbridge Creek and the mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201380_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201380-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMitchell1988_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitchell1988-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Portsdown_Hill" title="Portsdown Hill">Portsdown Hill</a> dominates the skyline in the northern part of the city, and contains several large <a href="/wiki/Palmerston_Forts,_Portsmouth" title="Palmerston Forts, Portsmouth">Palmerston Forts</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> such as <a href="/wiki/Fort_Fareham" title="Fort Fareham">Fort Fareham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wallington,_Hampshire#Fort_Wallington" title="Wallington, Hampshire">Fort Wallington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Nelson,_Portsmouth" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Nelson, Portsmouth">Fort Nelson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Southwick" title="Fort Southwick">Fort Southwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Widley" title="Fort Widley">Fort Widley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Purbrook" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Purbrook">Fort Purbrook</a>. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatterson1985_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatterson1985-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201379,_80_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201379,_80-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Portsdown Hill is formed by a large band of <a href="/wiki/Chalk" title="Chalk">chalk</a>, while the rest of Portsea Island is composed of layers of <a href="/wiki/London_Clay" title="London Clay">London Clay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sand</a> (part of the <a href="/wiki/Bagshot_Formation" title="Bagshot Formation">Bagshot Formation</a>), formed principally during the late and early <a href="/wiki/Eocene" title="Eocene">Eocene</a> Epoch.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Northern areas of the city include <a href="/wiki/Stamshaw" title="Stamshaw">Stamshaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hilsea" title="Hilsea">Hilsea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copnor" title="Copnor">Copnor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cosham" title="Cosham">Cosham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drayton,_Portsmouth" class="mw-redirect" title="Drayton, Portsmouth">Drayton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farlington,_Hampshire" title="Farlington, Hampshire">Farlington</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Port_Solent" title="Port Solent">Port Solent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Other districts in Portsmouth include <a href="/wiki/North_End,_Hampshire" title="North End, Hampshire">North End</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fratton" title="Fratton">Fratton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The west of the city is mainly <a href="/wiki/Council_housing" class="mw-redirect" title="Council housing">council estates</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Buckland,_Portsmouth" title="Buckland, Portsmouth">Buckland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Landport" title="Landport">Landport</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portsea,_Portsmouth" class="mw-redirect" title="Portsea, Portsmouth">Portsea</a>. These were built to replace Victorian terraces destroyed by bombing in the Second World War.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> After the war the 2,000 acres (810&#160;ha) estate of <a href="/wiki/Leigh_Park" title="Leigh Park">Leigh Park</a> was built to solve the chronic housing shortage during the post-war reconstruction.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013160_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013160-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Since the early 2000s the estate has been entirely under the jurisdiction of <a href="/wiki/Havant_(borough)" class="mw-redirect" title="Havant (borough)">Havant Borough Council</a>, but Portsmouth City Council remains the landlord of these properties, making it the biggest landowner in Havant Borough.<sup id="cite_ref-Leigh_Park_history_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leigh_Park_history-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city\'s main station, <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_and_Southsea_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Portsmouth and Southsea railway station">Portsmouth and Southsea railway station</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> is located in the city centre, close to the <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Guildhall" title="Portsmouth Guildhall">Guildhall</a> and the Civic Offices.<sup id="cite_ref-guild_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guild-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Just to the south of the Guildhall is Guildhall Walk, a nightlife area with many pubs and clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Edinburgh Road contains the city\'s Roman Catholic cathedral and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Park,_Portsmouth" title="Victoria Park, Portsmouth">Victoria Park</a>, a 15 acres (6.1&#160;ha) park which opened in 1878.<sup id="cite_ref-vic_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vic-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:2008px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portsmouth_panorama_from_Portsdown_Hill.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of Portsmouth from Portsdown Hill. To the left lies Langstone Harbour along with Hayling Island, and to the right lies Portsmouth Harbour."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Portsmouth_panorama_from_Portsdown_Hill.jpg/2000px-Portsmouth_panorama_from_Portsdown_Hill.jpg" width="2000" height="147" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Portsmouth_panorama_from_Portsdown_Hill.jpg/3000px-Portsmouth_panorama_from_Portsdown_Hill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Portsmouth_panorama_from_Portsdown_Hill.jpg/4000px-Portsmouth_panorama_from_Portsdown_Hill.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7344" data-file-height="540" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portsmouth_panorama_from_Portsdown_Hill.jpg" title="File:Portsmouth panorama from Portsdown Hill.jpg"> </a></div>Panorama of Portsmouth from <a href="/wiki/Portsdown_Hill" title="Portsdown Hill">Portsdown Hill</a>. To the left lies <a href="/wiki/Langstone_Harbour" title="Langstone Harbour">Langstone Harbour</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Hayling_Island" title="Hayling Island">Hayling Island</a>, and to the right lies <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Harbour" title="Portsmouth Harbour">Portsmouth Harbour</a>.</div>\n</div></div>\n<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="Neighbouring_towns,_villages,_and_places" style="padding:3px"><table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit"><tbody><tr><th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2"><div id="Neighbouring_towns,_villages,_and_places" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><b>Neighbouring towns, villages, and places</b></div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em"><table role="presentation" style="width:100%; margin:0; text-align:center;"><tbody><tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Portchester" title="Portchester">Portchester</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Waterlooville" title="Waterlooville">Waterlooville</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Havant" title="Havant">Havant</a></td>\n</tr><tr>\n<td style="width:33%"><a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Harbour" title="Portsmouth Harbour">Portsmouth Harbour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gosport" title="Gosport">Gosport</a></td>\n<td style="width:33%;">\n<div><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Pfeil_oben.svg/14px-Pfeil_oben.svg.png" title="North" width="14" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Pfeil_oben.svg/21px-Pfeil_oben.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Pfeil_oben.svg/28px-Pfeil_oben.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="501" data-file-height="595" /></div>\n<div style="white-space:nowrap;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Pfeil_links.svg/17px-Pfeil_links.svg.png" title="West" width="17" height="14" style="vertical-align: middle" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Pfeil_links.svg/25px-Pfeil_links.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Pfeil_links.svg/33px-Pfeil_links.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="501" /><b style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:middle; margin:0.75em 1em">Portsmouth</b><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Pfeil_rechts.svg/17px-Pfeil_rechts.svg.png" title="East" width="17" height="14" style="vertical-align: middle" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Pfeil_rechts.svg/25px-Pfeil_rechts.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Pfeil_rechts.svg/33px-Pfeil_rechts.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="501" /></div>\n<div><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Pfeil_unten.svg/14px-Pfeil_unten.svg.png" title="South" width="14" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Pfeil_unten.svg/21px-Pfeil_unten.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Pfeil_unten.svg/28px-Pfeil_unten.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="501" data-file-height="595" /></div>\n</td>\n<td style="width:33%"><a href="/wiki/Langstone_Harbour" title="Langstone Harbour">Langstone Harbour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hayling_Island" title="Hayling Island">Hayling Island</a></td>\n</tr><tr>\n<td>The <a href="/wiki/Solent" title="Solent">Solent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a></td>\n<td>English Channel</td>\n</tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Being located on the south coast of England, Portsmouth has a mild <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>, receiving more sunshine than most of the British Isles. During winter, frosts are light and short-lived and snow quite rare, with temperatures rarely dropping below freezing, as the city is surrounded by water and densely populated, and Portsdown Hill protects the city from cold northerly winds.<sup id="cite_ref-rising_119-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rising-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The average maximum temperature in January is 10&#160;\xc2\xb0C (50&#160;\xc2\xb0F) with the average minimum being 5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (41&#160;\xc2\xb0F). The lowest temperature recorded is \xe2\x88\x928&#160;\xc2\xb0C (18&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-metextreme_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metextreme-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In summer a temperature of 30&#160;\xc2\xb0C (86&#160;\xc2\xb0F) can occasionally be attained, particularly in more sheltered spots. The average maximum temperature in July is 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (72&#160;\xc2\xb0F), with the average minimum being 15&#160;\xc2\xb0C (59&#160;\xc2\xb0F). The highest temperature recorded is 35&#160;\xc2\xb0C (95&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-metextreme_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metextreme-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> As it is located on the coast in <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East England</a>, the city receives more sunshine per annum than most of the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The city gets around 645 millimetres (25.4&#160;in) of rain a year, with a minimum of 1&#160;mm (0.04&#160;in) of rain reported on 103 days a year.<sup id="cite_ref-weather_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; style="background:#9fc;"><small>11.4&#160;\xc2\xb0C (52.5&#160;\xc2\xb0F)</small>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#cf9;"><small>13.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (56.3&#160;\xc2\xb0F)</small>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#ff9;"><small>15.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (59.5&#160;\xc2\xb0F)</small>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#ff9;"><small>16.8&#160;\xc2\xb0C (62.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F)</small>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#ff6;"><small>17.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (63.1&#160;\xc2\xb0F)</small>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#ff9;"><small>16.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C (61.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F)</small>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#cf9;"><small>14.4&#160;\xc2\xb0C (57.9&#160;\xc2\xb0F)</small>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#9fc;"><small>11.8&#160;\xc2\xb0C (53.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F)</small>\n</td>\n<td style="background:#9fc;"><small>12.8&#160;\xc2\xb0C (55.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F)</small>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Portsmouth, as the most densely populated city in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, is the only city whose population density exceeds that of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Population_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201316_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201316-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> As of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">2011 census</a>, the city had 205,400 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-Population_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BUA_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BUA-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> This equates to 5,100 people living in every square kilometre (0.4 sq.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>mi.), which is eleven times more than the regional average of 440 people per square kilometre and more than London, which has 4,900 people per square kilometre. The city used to be even more densely populated, with the 1951 census showing a population of 233,545.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDickinson1998390_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDickinson1998390-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> In a reversal of that decrease, the population of the city has been gradually increasing since the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> With about 860,000 residents, the <a href="/wiki/South_Hampshire" title="South Hampshire">South Hampshire built-up area</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of urban areas in the United Kingdom">fifth-largest urban area in England</a> and the largest in <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East England</a>, forming the centre of one of the United Kingdom\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of metropolitan areas in the United Kingdom">most populous metropolitan areas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city is predominantly white in terms of ethnicity, with 91.8% of the population belonging to this ethnic group.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Portsmouth\'s long association with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> means that it represents one of the most diverse cities in terms of the peoples of the British Isles.<sup id="cite_ref-hant_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hant-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, some of the largest and most well-established non-white communities have their roots with the Royal Navy, most notably the large <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a> community, principally from <a href="/wiki/British_Hong_Kong" title="British Hong Kong">British Hong Kong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hant_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hant-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Portsmouth\'s long industrial history in support of the Royal Navy has seen many people from across the British Isles move to Portsmouth to work in the factories and docks, the largest of these groups being Irish Catholics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaly201127_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaly201127-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> According to 2011 census, the ethnic breakdown of Portsmouth\'s population is as follows: 84.0% <a href="/wiki/White_British" title="White British">White British</a>, 3.8% <a href="/wiki/Other_White" title="Other White">Other White</a>, 1.3% <a href="/wiki/British_Chinese" title="British Chinese">Chinese</a>, 1.4% <a href="/wiki/British_Indian" title="British Indian">Indian</a>, 0.5% <a href="/wiki/British_Mixed-Race" class="mw-redirect" title="British Mixed-Race">Mixed-Race</a>, 1.8% <a href="/wiki/British_Bangladeshi" title="British Bangladeshi">Bangladeshi</a>, 0.5% <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">Other ethnic group</a>, 1.4% <a href="/wiki/Black_British" title="Black British">Black African</a>, 0.5% <a href="/wiki/Irish_migration_to_Great_Britain" title="Irish migration to Great Britain">White Irish</a>, 1.3% <a href="/wiki/British_Asian" title="British Asian">Other Asian</a>, 0.3% <a href="/wiki/British_Pakistani" class="mw-redirect" title="British Pakistani">Pakistani</a>, 0.3% <a href="/wiki/British_African-Caribbean_community" class="mw-redirect" title="British African-Caribbean community">Black Caribbean</a> and 0.1% <a href="/wiki/Black_British" title="Black British">Other Black</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Population2_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population2-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="overflow:auto">\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-size:90%; width:70%; border:0; text-align:center; line-height:120%;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="24" style="text-align:center;font-size:90%;"><a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">Population growth</a> in Portsmouth since 1310<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatterson1976_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatterson1976-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#9cc; color:navy; height:17px;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#fff; color:navy;">1310\n</th>\n<th style="background:#fff; color:navy;">1560\n</th>\n<th style="background:#fff; color:navy;">1801\n</th>\n<th style="background:#fff; color:navy;">1851\n</th>\n<th style="background:#fff; color:navy;">1901\n</th>\n<th style="background:#fff; color:navy;">1951\n</th>\n<th style="background:#fff; color:navy;">1961\n</th>\n<th style="background:#fff; color:navy;">1971\n</th>\n<th style="background:#fff; color:navy;">1981\n</th>\n<th style="background:#fff; color:navy;">1991\n</th>\n<th style="background:#fff; color:navy;">2001\n</th>\n<th style="background:#fff; color:navy;">2011\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<th style="background:#9cc; color:navy; height:17px;">Population\n</th>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">740 (est)\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">1000 (est)\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">32,160\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">72,096\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">188,133\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">233,545\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">215,077\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">197,431\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">175,382\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">177,142\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">186,700\n</td>\n<td style="background:#fff; color:black;">205,400\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portsmouth_Guildhall_2014.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A front facing view of the Portsmouth Guildhall and the surrounding Civic Offices." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Portsmouth_Guildhall_2014.JPG/220px-Portsmouth_Guildhall_2014.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Portsmouth_Guildhall_2014.JPG/330px-Portsmouth_Guildhall_2014.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Portsmouth_Guildhall_2014.JPG/440px-Portsmouth_Guildhall_2014.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5096" data-file-height="3392" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portsmouth_Guildhall_2014.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The neo-classical <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Guildhall" title="Portsmouth Guildhall">Portsmouth Guildhall</a> and surrounding Civic Offices are the centre of government in the city.</div></div></div>\n<p>The city is administered by <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_City_Council" title="Portsmouth City Council">Portsmouth City Council</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a> which is responsible for local affairs. Portsmouth was granted its first charter in 1194.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> In the early 20th century, the boundaries were extended to include the whole of Portsea Island; they were further extended in 1920 and 1932, taking in areas of the mainland and adjacent villages which included <a href="/wiki/Drayton,_Portsmouth" class="mw-redirect" title="Drayton, Portsmouth">Drayton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Farlington,_Hampshire" title="Farlington, Hampshire">Farlington</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-plan_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plan-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> From 1 April 1974 it formed the second tier of local government below <a href="/wiki/Hampshire_County_Council" title="Hampshire County Council">Hampshire County Council</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> however, Portsmouth, along with Southampton, became administratively independent of Hampshire with the creation of the unitary authority on 1 April 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201318_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201318-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> The city is divided into two parliamentary constituencies, <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_South" class="mw-redirect" title="Portsmouth South">Portsmouth South</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_North" class="mw-redirect" title="Portsmouth North">Portsmouth North</a>, represented in the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a> by, respectively, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Morgan_(U.K._politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen Morgan (U.K. politician)">Stephen Morgan</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Penny_Mordaunt" title="Penny Mordaunt">Penny Mordaunt</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city council is made up of 42 councillors. After the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_local_elections,_2018" title="United Kingdom local elections, 2018">May 2018 local elections</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> formed a minority administration with 16 councillors, supported by Labour with 5 councillors. The Conservatives have 19, including the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor">Lord Mayor</a>, Lee Mason.<sup id="cite_ref-ward_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ward-166">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> There are also two <a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">independent</a> councillors.  Councillors are returned from 14<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>wards, with each ward having three councillors<sup id="cite_ref-ward_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ward-166">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> and a four-year term.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> The leader of the council is the Liberal Democrat, <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Vernon-Jackson" title="Gerald Vernon-Jackson">Gerald Vernon-Jackson</a>. The position of Lord Mayor of Portsmouth is usually held for a one-year period.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The council is based in the Civic Offices, which house departments such as tax support, housing benefits, resident services, and municipal functions.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> They are situated in Guildhall Square, along with <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Guildhall" title="Portsmouth Guildhall">Portsmouth Guildhall</a> and Portsmouth Central Library. The Guildhall is a symbol of Portsmouth, serving principally as a cultural venue. It was designed by <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>-based architect <a href="/wiki/William_Hill_(architect)" title="William Hill (architect)">William Hill</a>, who first started constructing it in the <a href="/wiki/Neo-classicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-classicism">neo-classical style</a> in 1873 at the cost of \xc2\xa3140,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013146_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013146-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> The Guildhall was opened to the public in 1890.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vehicles_lining_up_to_embark_at_the_continental_ferry_port,_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_499738.jpg" class="image"><img alt="In this photograph, many large containers and other cargo are lined up in the city&#39;s ferry port. A ferry can be seen docked in the background." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Vehicles_lining_up_to_embark_at_the_continental_ferry_port%2C_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_499738.jpg/220px-Vehicles_lining_up_to_embark_at_the_continental_ferry_port%2C_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_499738.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Vehicles_lining_up_to_embark_at_the_continental_ferry_port%2C_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_499738.jpg/330px-Vehicles_lining_up_to_embark_at_the_continental_ferry_port%2C_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_499738.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Vehicles_lining_up_to_embark_at_the_continental_ferry_port%2C_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_499738.jpg/440px-Vehicles_lining_up_to_embark_at_the_continental_ferry_port%2C_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_499738.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vehicles_lining_up_to_embark_at_the_continental_ferry_port,_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_499738.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portsmouth Continental Ferry Port serves as one of the city\'s major industries.</div></div></div>\n<p>A tenth of the city\'s workforce is employed at <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Portsmouth" title="HMNB Portsmouth">Portsmouth Naval Dockyard</a>, which is directly linked to the city\'s biggest industry, defence, with the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Surface_Ships" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Systems Surface Ships">BAE Systems Surface Ships</a> located in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> BAE\'s Portsmouth shipyard has been awarded a share of the construction work on the two new <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class&#x20;aircraft carriers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> with both aircraft carriers set to enter Portsmouth Harbour upon completion.<sup id="cite_ref-tel_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tel-175">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> A \xc2\xa3100 million contract was signed to develop the facilities at Portsmouth that will be necessary to support the vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-tel_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tel-175">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> There is also a major ferry port that handles both passengers and cargo,<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> and the city has a dedicated fishing fleet consisting of 20 to 30 boats that operate out of the camber docks in Camber Quay, <a href="/wiki/Old_Portsmouth" title="Old Portsmouth">Old Portsmouth</a>. They land fresh fish and shellfish daily, most of which is sold at the quayside fish market.<sup id="cite_ref-fish_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fish-177">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city is host to the European headquarters of <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> and, until 2007, the UK headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Financial_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich Financial Services">Zurich Financial Services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history2_22-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history2-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> In the city centre, shopping is centred on Commercial Road and the 1980s Cascades Shopping Centre, with over 100 high street shops between them.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Approximately 185,000 to 230,000 people use the Cascades Shopping Centre each week.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Recent redevelopment has created new shopping areas, including the upmarket <a href="/wiki/Gunwharf_Quays" title="Gunwharf Quays">Gunwharf Quays</a>\xe2\x80\x94a redevelopment of the <a href="/wiki/HMS_Vernon_(shore_establishment)" title="HMS Vernon (shore establishment)">naval shore establishment HMS <i>Vernon</i></a>\xe2\x80\x94<sup id="cite_ref-guns_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guns-182">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-quays_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quays-183">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> containing fashion stores, restaurants, and a cinema, and the Historic Dockyard, which caters to the tourist sector and holds an annual Victorian <a href="/wiki/Christmas_market" title="Christmas market">Christmas market</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gun_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gun-185">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Ocean Retail Park sits on the north-eastern side of Portsea Island and was built on land previously occupied by a Metal Box factory in September 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_in_Rosyth_Dockyard_MOD_45158229.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier docked in Scotland. This ship is one of two planned aircraft carriers and will soon make its way to Portsmouth Harbour, its home port." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_in_Rosyth_Dockyard_MOD_45158229.jpg/220px-HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_in_Rosyth_Dockyard_MOD_45158229.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_in_Rosyth_Dockyard_MOD_45158229.jpg/330px-HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_in_Rosyth_Dockyard_MOD_45158229.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_in_Rosyth_Dockyard_MOD_45158229.jpg/440px-HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_in_Rosyth_Dockyard_MOD_45158229.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1350" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_in_Rosyth_Dockyard_MOD_45158229.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portsmouth will be the home port of the two <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class&#x20;aircraft carriers</a>, the largest ships ever built by the Royal Navy.</div></div></div>\n<p>Development at Gunwharf Quays continued until 2007 with the completion of the 330-foot (101&#160;m) tall No.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>1 Gunwharf Quays residential tower (nicknamed \'Lipstick Tower\').<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The development of the former Brickwoods Brewery site included the construction of a 22-storey tower known as the Admiralty Quarter Tower, the tallest in a complex of mostly low-rise residential buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> A new 25-storey tower named \'Number One Portsmouth\', was made public at the end of October 2008, which has been proposed at a height of 330 feet (101&#160;m), and will stand opposite Portsmouth &amp; Southsea Station.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> As of August 2009, internal demolition has started on the building that currently occupies the site.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> A new student accommodation tower, nicknamed \'The Blade\', has started construction on the site of the old Victoria swimming baths, on the edge of Victoria Park. The tower will stand over 300 feet (91&#160;m), and will become Portsmouth\'s second tallest structure after the Spinnaker Tower.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>In April 2007, Portsmouth F.C. announced plans to move away from <a href="/wiki/Fratton_Park" title="Fratton Park">Fratton Park</a> to a new stadium situated on a piece of reclaimed land beside the Historic Dockyard, nicknamed <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Dockland_Stadium" title="Portsmouth Dockland Stadium">Portsmouth Dockland Stadium</a>. The \xc2\xa3600 million mixed-use development, designed by architects <a href="/wiki/Herzog_%26_de_Meuron" title="Herzog &amp; de Meuron">Herzog &amp; de Meuron</a>, would also include 1500 harbourside apartments as well as shops and offices.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> The scheme attracted criticism due to its large size and location, with some officials saying that it would interfere with harbour operations.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The \xc2\xa3600 million project for a new stadium was rejected by the city council due to the financial crisis of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Portsmouth will help build, and be the home port of, two new <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class&#x20;aircraft carriers</a>: <a href="/wiki/HMS_Queen_Elizabeth_(R08)" title="HMS Queen Elizabeth (R08)">HMS&#160;<i>Queen Elizabeth</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Prince_of_Wales_(R09)" title="HMS Prince of Wales (R09)">HMS&#160;<i>Prince of Wales</i></a>, the largest ships ever built by the Royal Navy.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> The supercarriers were first ordered by then Defence Secretary <a href="/wiki/Des_Browne" title="Des Browne">Des Browne</a> on 25 July 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Construction of both ships took place in the Firth of Forth at <a href="/wiki/Rosyth_Dockyard" title="Rosyth Dockyard">Rosyth Dockyard</a> and <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Surface_Ships" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Systems Surface Ships">BAE Systems Surface Ships</a> in Glasgow, <a href="/wiki/Babcock_International" title="Babcock International">Babcock International</a> at Rosyth, and at HMNB Portsmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> It was announced by the government prior to the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Independence_Referendum" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Independence Referendum">Scottish Independence Referendum</a> that military shipbuilding would end in Portsmouth, with all UK surface warship shipbuilding to be focused instead at the two older BAE facilities in Glasgow.<sup id="cite_ref-end_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-end-202">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> This was heavily criticised at the time as a political rather than economic decision to help the "No campaign" for Scotland to remain a part of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gunwharf_Quays_Vernon_Avenue.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A view of some shops in the Gunwharf Quays shopping centre." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Gunwharf_Quays_Vernon_Avenue.JPG/220px-Gunwharf_Quays_Vernon_Avenue.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Gunwharf_Quays_Vernon_Avenue.JPG/330px-Gunwharf_Quays_Vernon_Avenue.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Gunwharf_Quays_Vernon_Avenue.JPG/440px-Gunwharf_Quays_Vernon_Avenue.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gunwharf_Quays_Vernon_Avenue.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gunwharf_Quays" title="Gunwharf Quays">Gunwharf Quays</a> shopping centre</div></div></div>\n<p>Portsmouth has several theatres: the <a href="/wiki/New_Theatre_Royal" title="New Theatre Royal">New Theatre Royal</a> in Guildhall Walk, near the city centre, which specialises in professional drama,<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> and the newly restored Kings Theatre in Southsea, which features amateur musicals as well a number of national tours.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Another theatre is the Groundlings Theatre, which was built in 1784 and is housed in The Old Beneficial School, Portsea.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> New Prince\'s Theatre and Southsea\'s Kings Theatre were both designed by Victorian architect and entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Frank_Matcham" title="Frank Matcham">Frank Matcham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city also has three established music venues: the Guildhall,<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Wedgewood_Rooms" title="The Wedgewood Rooms">The Wedgewood Rooms</a> (which includes a smaller venue, Edge of the Wedge),<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Pyramids_Centre" title="Portsmouth Pyramids Centre">Portsmouth Pyramids Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Guildhall" title="Portsmouth Guildhall">Portsmouth Guildhall</a>, another theatrical venue, is one of the largest events venue in South East England, with a <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> of 2500.<sup id="cite_ref-guild_90-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guild-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> For many years a series of symphony concerts has been presented at the Guildhall by the <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Bournemouth Symphony Orchestra">Bournemouth Symphony Orchestra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> In the 1970s the <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Sinfonia" title="Portsmouth Sinfonia">Portsmouth Sinfonia</a> approached classical music from a different angle: the Sinfonia often recruited players that had <a href="/wiki/Outsider_music" title="Outsider music">no musical training</a> or, if they were musicians, ones that chose to play an instrument that was entirely new to them.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> The Portsmouth Summer Show is held at <a href="/wiki/King_George%27s_Fields" title="King George&#39;s Fields">King George\'s Fields</a>. The 2016 event was held in the last weekend of April, and featured cover bands such as the Silver Beatles, the Bog Rolling Stones, and Fleetingwood Mac.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Numerous musical works are set in the city. <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Point_(Walton)" title="Portsmouth Point (Walton)"><i>Portsmouth Point</i></a> is an <a href="/wiki/Overture" title="Overture">overture</a> for orchestra by the English composer <a href="/wiki/William_Walton" title="William Walton">William Walton</a> in 1925. The work was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Rowlandson" title="Thomas Rowlandson">Thomas Rowlandson</a>\'s etching depicting Portsmouth Point, otherwise known as "Spice Island" in Old Portsmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> The overture was used for the BBC Proms Concert in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/H.M.S._Pinafore" title="H.M.S. Pinafore">H.M.S. Pinafore</a></i> is a comic opera in two acts set in Portsmouth Harbour, with music by Arthur Sullivan and libretto by W.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>S. Gilbert.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStedman1996157\xe2\x80\x93158_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStedman1996157\xe2\x80\x93158-221">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Cranko" title="John Cranko">John Cranko</a>\'s 1951 ballet <i><a href="/wiki/Pineapple_Poll" title="Pineapple Poll">Pineapple Poll</a></i>, which features the operetta music of <i>The Bumboat Woman\'s Story</i> by <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Sullivan" title="Gilbert and Sullivan">Gilbert and Sullivan</a>, is also set in Portsmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Portsmouth hosts yearly remembrances of the <a href="/wiki/D-Day_landings" class="mw-redirect" title="D-Day landings">D-Day landings</a>, which veterans from Allied and Commonwealth nations attend.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> The city played a major part in the 50th D-Day anniversary in 1994; visitors included then-US President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, Australian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Paul_Keating" title="Paul Keating">Paul Keating</a>, King <a href="/wiki/Harald_V_of_Norway" title="Harald V of Norway">Harald V of Norway</a>, French president <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Mitterrand" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Mitterrand">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Mitterrand</a>, New Zealand Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jim_Bolger" title="Jim Bolger">Jim Bolger</a>, Canadian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jean_Chr%C3%A9tien" title="Jean Chr\xc3\xa9tien">Jean Chr\xc3\xa9tien</a>, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">John Major</a>, the Queen and the Duke of Edinburgh.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> The Portsmouth International Kite Festival is organised annually by Portsmouth City Council and The Kite Society of Great Britain. It celebrated its 25th anniversary in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In literature, Portsmouth is the chief location for <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Meades" title="Jonathan Meades">Jonathan Meades</a>\' 1993 novel <i>Pompey</i>, in which it is inhabited largely by <a href="/wiki/Incest" title="Incest">incestuous</a> and <a href="/wiki/Necrophilia" title="Necrophilia">necrophiliac</a> criminals.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Since the release of his novel, Meades has presented a TV programme documenting Victorian architecture in Portsmouth Dockyard.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Jane_Austen" title="Jane Austen">Jane Austen</a>\'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Mansfield_Park" title="Mansfield Park">Mansfield Park</a></i>, Portsmouth is the hometown of the main character Fanny Price, and is the setting of most of the closing chapters of the novel.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a>\' novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Life_and_Adventures_of_Nicholas_Nickleby" class="mw-redirect" title="The Life and Adventures of Nicholas Nickleby">The Life and Adventures of Nicholas Nickleby</a></i>, main protagonists Nicholas and Smike make their way to Portsmouth and get involved in a theatrical troupe.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Patrick_O%27Brian" title="Patrick O&#39;Brian">Patrick O\'Brian</a>\'s nautical historical <a href="/wiki/Aubrey-Maturin_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Aubrey-Maturin series">Aubrey-Maturin series</a>, Portsmouth is most often the port from which Captain Jack Aubrey\'s ships sail.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Victorian novelist and historian <a href="/wiki/Sir_Walter_Besant" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Walter Besant">Sir Walter Besant</a> documented his childhood in the town in the 1840s in <i>By Celia\'s Arbour: A Tale of Portsmouth Town</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> The book is notable for its precise descriptions of the town before the defensive walls were removed.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Southsea features in <i><a href="/wiki/The_History_of_Mr_Polly" title="The History of Mr Polly">The History of Mr Polly</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/H._G._Wells" title="H. G. Wells">H. G. Wells</a> under the fictional name of <i>Port Burdock</i>, which he describes as "one of the three townships that are grouped around the Port Burdock naval dockyards".<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/High_fantasy" title="High fantasy">High fantasy</a> author <a href="/wiki/Neil_Gaiman" title="Neil Gaiman">Neil Gaiman</a> also sets his graphic novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tragical_Comedy_or_Comical_Tragedy_of_Mr._Punch" title="The Tragical Comedy or Comical Tragedy of Mr. Punch">The Tragical Comedy or Comical Tragedy of Mr. Punch</a></i> around Southsea, Gaiman having grown up in Portsmouth. A street along the seafront in Southsea was renamed "The Ocean at the End of the Lane" by the city council in honour of his <a href="/wiki/The_Ocean_at_the_End_of_the_Lane" title="The Ocean at the End of the Lane">novel of the same name</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Notable crime novels set in Portsmouth and the surrounding area include <a href="/wiki/Graham_Hurley" title="Graham Hurley">Graham Hurley</a>\'s D.I.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Faraday/D.C.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Winter novels<sup id="cite_ref-graham_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-graham-239">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/C._J._Sansom" title="C. J. Sansom">C. J. Sansom</a>\'s Tudor crime novel <i>Heartstone</i>, with the latter including references to the famous warship <i>Mary Rose</i> and descriptions of Tudor life in the town.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> A collection of fantastical short stories, <i>Portsmouth Fairy Tales for Grown Ups</i>, was published in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> It uses locations around Portsmouth for the stories, and includes writing by crime novelists William Sutton, Diana Bretherick, and others.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Portsmouth" title="List of schools in Portsmouth">List of schools in Portsmouth</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Park_Building,_University_of_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_548659.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A side-facing view of the Park Building, one of the buildings which make up the University of Portsmouth" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Park_Building%2C_University_of_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_548659.jpg/170px-Park_Building%2C_University_of_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_548659.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Park_Building%2C_University_of_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_548659.jpg/255px-Park_Building%2C_University_of_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_548659.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Park_Building%2C_University_of_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_548659.jpg/340px-Park_Building%2C_University_of_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_548659.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Park_Building,_University_of_Portsmouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_548659.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Park Building, University of Portsmouth</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Portsmouth" title="University of Portsmouth">University of Portsmouth</a> was founded in 1992 as a <a href="/wiki/New_university" title="New university">new university</a> from the existing Portsmouth Polytechnic; it has 20,000 students on campus as of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> The university was ranked among the top 100 modern universities in the world in April 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Gurney_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gurney-246">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uopnews_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uopnews-247">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> As of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the university had approximately 23,000 students and more than 2500 staff.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013198_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013198-248">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> Several local colleges also have the power to award <a href="/wiki/Higher_National_Diploma" title="Higher National Diploma">Higher National Diplomas</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Highbury_College" title="Highbury College">Highbury College</a>, which specialises in vocational education,<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> and Portsmouth College, which offers various academic courses in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> Both <a href="/wiki/Admiral_Lord_Nelson_School" title="Admiral Lord Nelson School">Admiral Lord Nelson School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miltoncross_Academy" title="Miltoncross Academy">Miltoncross Academy</a> were built in the late 1990s to meet the demand of a growing school-age population.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the cancellation of the national building programme for schools, these redevelopments did not go ahead.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, only two schools in the city were judged "inadequate", whereas 29 of the city\'s 63 schools were considered "no longer good enough" by <a href="/wiki/Ofsted" title="Ofsted">Ofsted</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> Before being taken over by <a href="/wiki/Ark_(charity)" title="Ark (charity)">Ark Schools</a> and becoming a <a href="/wiki/Charter_Academy" title="Charter Academy">Charter Academy</a>, St<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Luke\'s Church of England secondary school was, in terms of GCSE achievement, one of the worst schools in the country. It was also criticised by officials for its behavioural standards&#160;&#8211;&#32;reports were made of students repeatedly throwing chairs at teachers.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> Since becoming an academy in 2009, the schools have significantly improved; 69% of students achieved five GCSEs at grades A*&#160;&#8211;&#160;C including English and mathematics.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> Charter Academy operates its intake policy as a standard comprehensive taking from its catchment area rather than selecting on religious background.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is also a cohort of independent schools within the city&#160;&#8211;&#32;the oldest, founded in 1732 by the Mayor of Portsmouth,<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013200_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013200-259">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Grammar_School" title="Portsmouth Grammar School">Portsmouth Grammar School</a>, which has been rated as one of the best private schools in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013200_259-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013200-259">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_High_School_(Southsea)" class="mw-redirect" title="Portsmouth High School (Southsea)">Portsmouth High School</a>, a member of the Girls Day School Trust, was ranked one of the top private schools for girls in the UK by A-level results in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> Other independent schools in the city include <a href="/wiki/Mayville_High_School_(England)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayville High School (England)">Mayville High School</a>, founded in 1897,<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/St_John%27s_College_(Portsmouth)" class="mw-redirect" title="St John&#39;s College (Portsmouth)">St John\'s College</a>, an independent Catholic boarding school.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013201_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013201-264">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Warrior_and_Spinnaker_Tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A view of the port side of HMS Warrior alongside Portsmouth Harbour. The Spinnaker Tower can be seen to the far left." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/HMS_Warrior_and_Spinnaker_Tower.jpg/220px-HMS_Warrior_and_Spinnaker_Tower.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/HMS_Warrior_and_Spinnaker_Tower.jpg/330px-HMS_Warrior_and_Spinnaker_Tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/HMS_Warrior_and_Spinnaker_Tower.jpg/440px-HMS_Warrior_and_Spinnaker_Tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Warrior_and_Spinnaker_Tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMS_Warrior_(1860)" title="HMS Warrior (1860)">HMS&#160;<i>Warrior</i></a> (right) and the <a href="/wiki/Spinnaker_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Spinnaker Tower">Spinnaker Tower</a> (left) are among the city\'s main attractions.</div></div></div>\n<p>Many of the city\'s former defences are now museums, or venues for hosting events. Several of the Victorian era forts on Portsdown Hill are now tourist attractions:<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fort_Nelson,_Hampshire" title="Fort Nelson, Hampshire">Fort Nelson</a>, which lies on the summit of Portsdown Hill, is home to the Royal Armouries museum.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> The Tudor era <a href="/wiki/Southsea_Castle" title="Southsea Castle">Southsea Castle</a> has a small museum, and much of the seafront defences leading up to the <a href="/wiki/Round_Tower_(Portsmouth)" title="Round Tower (Portsmouth)">Round Tower</a> are open to the public. The castle was withdrawn from active service in 1960 and was subsequently purchased by Portsmouth City Council.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> The southern part of the Royal Marines\' <a href="/wiki/Eastney_Barracks" title="Eastney Barracks">Eastney Barracks</a> is now the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines_Museum" title="Royal Marines Museum">Royal Marines Museum</a>, and was opened to the public under the <a href="/wiki/National_Heritage_Act_1983" class="mw-redirect" title="National Heritage Act 1983">National Heritage Act 1983</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> The museum was awarded a \xc2\xa314 million grant from the National Lottery Fund, and is set to relocate to the Portsmouth Historic Dockyard in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> The birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a> at Mile End Terrace,<sup id="cite_ref-dickens_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dickens-270">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201373_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201373-271">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> is now the <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens_Birthplace_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Dickens Birthplace Museum">Charles Dickens Birthplace Museum</a>. The four-storey red brick building became a Grade<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>I listed building in 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> Other tourist attractions include the Blue Reef Aquarium, which houses an "underwater safari" of aquatic life in Britain,<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> and Cumberland House Natural History Museum, which features a variety of wildlife featured in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Victory.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A picture of HMS Victory, the world&#39;s oldest commissioned naval ship, situated in Portsmouth&#39;s dry dock. The ship itself is missing its figurehead in this photo but retains its original sails." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/HMS_Victory.jpg/220px-HMS_Victory.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/HMS_Victory.jpg/330px-HMS_Victory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/HMS_Victory.jpg/440px-HMS_Victory.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Victory.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMS_Victory" title="HMS Victory">HMS&#160;<i>Victory</i></a> at Portsmouth Historic Dockyard is the world\'s oldest naval ship still in commission and is one of the city\'s most popular tourist attractions.</div></div></div>\n<p>Most of the city\'s landmarks and tourist attractions are related to its naval history. Among the attractions are the <a href="/wiki/D-Day_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="D-Day Museum">D-Day Museum</a> and the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Overlord_embroidery" title="Overlord embroidery">Overlord embroidery</a> in Southsea, which was awarded a grant of \xc2\xa34 million by the <a href="/wiki/Heritage_Lottery_Fund" title="Heritage Lottery Fund">Heritage Lottery Fund</a> to expand it in time for 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> The museum\'s embroidery is 83 metres (272&#160;ft) long, making it the longest of its kind in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013156_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013156-277">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> The city is home to some famous ships: in the dry dock of <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Historic_Dockyard" title="Portsmouth Historic Dockyard">Portsmouth Historic Dockyard</a> lies Horatio Nelson\'s flagship, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Victory" title="HMS Victory">HMS&#160;<i>Victory</i></a>, the world\'s oldest naval ship still in commission. HMS <i>Victory</i> was preserved for the nation and placed in permanent dry dock in 1922, when the <a href="/wiki/Society_for_Nautical_Research" title="Society for Nautical Research">Society for Nautical Research</a> led a national appeal to restore her.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201339_75-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201339-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> 22<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million people have visited her since.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> In 1971, the remains of Henry VIII\'s flagship, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Rose" title="Mary Rose"><i>Mary Rose</i></a>, was rediscovered on the seabed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201337_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201337-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> She was raised and brought into a purpose-built structure in Portsmouth Historic Dockyard in 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-rose_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rose-279">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> Britain\'s first iron-hulled warship, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Warrior_(1860)" title="HMS Warrior (1860)">HMS&#160;<i>Warrior</i></a>, was restored and moved to Portsmouth in June 1987 after serving as an oil fuel pier at <a href="/wiki/Pembroke_Dock" title="Pembroke Dock">Pembroke Dock</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pembrokeshire" title="Pembrokeshire">Pembrokeshire</a> for fifty years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201342_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201342-280">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinton19875_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinton19875-282">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_the_Royal_Navy" title="National Museum of the Royal Navy">National Museum of the Royal Navy</a> is also in the historic dockyard, and is sponsored by an independent charity which aims to promote research into the history and archaeology of the Royal Dockyard.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> Every November the Historic Dockyard hosts the Victorian Festival of Christmas, which features <a href="/wiki/Father_Christmas" title="Father Christmas">Father Christmas</a> in a traditional green-coloured robe.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Portsmouth\'s long association with the armed forces means it has a large number of war memorials around the city, including several at the Royal Marines Museum,<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> and a large collection of memorials related to the Royal Navy in <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Park,_Portsmouth" title="Victoria Park, Portsmouth">Victoria Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vic_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vic-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Naval_Memorial" title="Portsmouth Naval Memorial">Portsmouth Naval Memorial</a> in Southsea Common commemorates 24,591 fallen soldiers who lost their lives in the First World War.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013135_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013135-287">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> The memorial was designed by Sir <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lorimer" title="Robert Lorimer">Robert Lorimer</a> and was unveiled by <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">George VI</a> on 15 October 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> In the city centre, the Guildhall Square Cenotaph displays the names of the fallen, and is guarded by stone sculptures of machine gunners carved by the sculptor Charles Jagger.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> On the west face, the description reads: \n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>This memorial was erected by the people of Portsmouth in proud and loving memory of those who in the glorious morning of their days for England\'s sake lost all but England\'s praise. May light perpetual shine upon them.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Portsmouth contains three cemeteries: Kingston, Milton Road, and Highland Road. Kingston Cemetery was opened in 1856 and lies on the eastern side of Fratton. At 52 acres (21&#160;ha), it is the largest cemetery in the city and has about 400 burials a year.<sup id="cite_ref-cemeteries_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cemeteries-291">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> In February 2014, a ceremony was held at the cemetery to celebrate the 180th anniversary of Portsmouth\'s Polish community.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> Milton Road Cemetery, of some 25 acres (10&#160;ha), was established on 8 April 1912 and has approximately 200 burials per year. There is also a crematorium at Portchester.<sup id="cite_ref-cemeteries_291-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cemeteries-291">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gunwharf_Quays">Gunwharf Quays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Gunwharf Quays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gunwharf_Quays" title="Gunwharf Quays">Gunwharf Quays</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spinnaker_Tower_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A view of the Spinnaker Tower from the ground at Gunwharf Quays. The tower itself resembles a sail, reflecting Portsmouth&#39;s maritime history." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Spinnaker_Tower_2014.jpg/170px-Spinnaker_Tower_2014.jpg" width="170" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Spinnaker_Tower_2014.jpg/255px-Spinnaker_Tower_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Spinnaker_Tower_2014.jpg/340px-Spinnaker_Tower_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1836" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spinnaker_Tower_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of the <a href="/wiki/Spinnaker_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Spinnaker Tower">Spinnaker Tower</a> from the waterfront at <a href="/wiki/Gunwharf_Quays" title="Gunwharf Quays">Gunwharf Quays</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/HMS_Vernon_(shore_establishment)" title="HMS Vernon (shore establishment)">The naval shore establishment, HMS <i>Vernon</i></a>, contained the Royal Navy\'s arsenal&#160;&#8211;&#32;weapons and ammunition would be taken from ships as they entered the harbour and would be resupplied as they headed out to sea. The 1919 <i>Southsea and Portsmouth Official Guide</i> described the establishment as "the finest collections of weapons outside the Tower of London, containing more than 25,000 rifles".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013185,_186_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013185,_186-293">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> In the early nineteenth century, Gunwharf Quays supplied the fleet with a "grand arsenal" consisting of cannons, mortars, bombs, and various ordinance.
