Gunpowder was not provided due to safety concerns; however, it could be obtained at Pridday\'s Hard near Gosport.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen2015123_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen2015123-294">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> An armoury existed to sell small arms to soldiers, along with blacksmith and carpenter shops for armourers. The establishment was run by three officers; a <i>viz</i> (storekeeper), a clerk, and a foreman. By 1817, Gunwharf purportedly housed the largest naval arsenal in the world, employing 5000 men at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen2015123,_124_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen2015123,_124-295">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>HMS <i>Vernon</i> closed on 1 April 1996<sup id="cite_ref-vernon_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vernon-296">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> and was redeveloped by Portsmouth City Council as Gunwharf Quays,<sup id="cite_ref-guns_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guns-182">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> a mixed residential and retail destination with outlet stores, restaurants, pubs, and caf\xc3\xa9s.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> Construction of the <a href="/wiki/Spinnaker_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Spinnaker Tower">Spinnaker Tower</a> began in 2001 and was completed in summer 2005. The project ran overbudget and cost \xc2\xa336<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million, of which Portsmouth City Council contributed \xc2\xa311 million.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013232_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013232-300">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> The 560 feet (170&#160;m) tower is visible from 23 miles (37&#160;km) on a clear day, and its viewing platforms provide views across the Solent towards the Isle of Wight, and north towards the harbour and Southsea Castle.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013233_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013233-302">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> The tower has the largest glass floor in Europe and weighs more than 33,000 tonnes (32,000 long tons; 36,000 short tons).<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013233_302-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013233-302">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Southsea">Southsea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Southsea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Southsea" title="Southsea">Southsea</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Southsea_Clarence_Pier.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A view of the Southsea Promenade, which contains arcades, restaurants, cinemas and a pier (which cannot be seen in this photograph)." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Southsea_Clarence_Pier.jpg/220px-Southsea_Clarence_Pier.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Southsea_Clarence_Pier.jpg/330px-Southsea_Clarence_Pier.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Southsea_Clarence_Pier.jpg/440px-Southsea_Clarence_Pier.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Southsea_Clarence_Pier.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of Southsea Promenade, which includes the <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Pier" title="Clarence Pier">Clarence Pier</a> amusement park</div></div></div>\n<p>Southsea is a <a href="/wiki/Seaside_resort" title="Seaside resort">seaside resort</a> and residential area that lies at the southern end of Portsea Island. The name Southsea originates from Southsea Castle, a castle on the seafront established in 1544 by Henry<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>VIII to help defend the <a href="/wiki/Solent" title="Solent">Solent</a> and approaches to Portsmouth Harbour.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> The area was originally developed in 1809 as "Croxton Town", though by the 1860s the suburb of Southsea had expanded to provide houses for working-class people.<sup id="cite_ref-pissea_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pissea-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> During this time, Southsea grew as a seaside and bathing resort.<sup id="cite_ref-pissea_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pissea-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> A pump room and baths were erected near the present day <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Pier" title="Clarence Pier">Clarence Pier</a>, and a large complex was developed including vapour baths, showers, and card playing and assembly rooms for holiday-goers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuail200016\xe2\x80\x9317_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuail200016\xe2\x80\x9317-305">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clarence Pier was officially opened in 1861 by the Prince and Princess of Wales, and was named after the once military governor of Portsmouth, <a href="/wiki/Lord_Frederick_FitzClarence" title="Lord Frederick FitzClarence">Lord Frederick FitzClarence</a>. At the time of its opening, the pier was labelled as "one of the largest amusement parks on the south coast".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013140_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013140-306">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Parade_Pier" title="South Parade Pier">South Parade Pier</a> was built in 1878 and is among the 55 remaining private piers in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013138_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013138-307">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuail200046_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuail200046-308">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> The pier was originally used as a terminal for ferries travelling to the Isle of Wight, but it was soon redeveloped as a centre of entertainment. It had to be rebuilt after the first fire in 1904, and rebuilt again after the second fire in 1967. The third fire struck during filming of Tommy in 1974, after which it was rebuilt once again.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013138_307-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013138-307">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pissea_124-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pissea-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, plans were unveiled to build the "Solent Eye" at the pier, an amusement ride with 24 gondolas resembling the <a href="/wiki/London_Eye" title="London Eye">London Eye</a>, at a cost of \xc2\xa3750,000.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Southsea is dominated by Southsea Common, a grassland covering an area of 480 acres (190&#160;ha), which was first created by draining the marshland alongside the construction of the vapour baths in 1820. The common owes its existence to the demands of the military in the early 19th century for a clear range of fire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuail200019\xe2\x80\x9320_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuail200019\xe2\x80\x9320-310">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> The present day Common lies parallel to the shore from Clarence Pier to Southsea Castle.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuail200019\xe2\x80\x9320_310-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuail200019\xe2\x80\x9320-310">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> Today, the Common is a popular recreation ground, and also a venue for a number of annual events, which includes carnivals, Christmas markets, and Victorian festivals.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013136_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013136-312">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> The common also has a large collection of mature <a href="/wiki/Elm" title="Elm">elm</a> trees, believed to be the oldest and largest surviving in Hampshire, which have escaped <a href="/wiki/Dutch_elm_disease" title="Dutch elm disease">Dutch elm disease</a> owing to their isolation. Other plants include the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Canary Island">Canary Island</a> date palms <i><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_canariensis" title="Phoenix canariensis">Phoenix canariensis</a></i>, which are some of the largest in Britain and have produced viable seed in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portsmouthcatholiccathedral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A front facing view of Portsmouth&#39;s Roman Catholic cathedral, St John the Evangelist. The cathedral itself is made of brick and has a large chancel and nave at the front. Stained windows are also seen above the front door." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Portsmouthcatholiccathedral.jpg/220px-Portsmouthcatholiccathedral.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Portsmouthcatholiccathedral.jpg/330px-Portsmouthcatholiccathedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Portsmouthcatholiccathedral.jpg/440px-Portsmouthcatholiccathedral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portsmouthcatholiccathedral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_St_John_the_Evangelist,_Portsmouth" title="Cathedral of St John the Evangelist, Portsmouth">St John the Evangelist</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> cathedral of worship, built in 1882. It is one of the two cathedrals of the city.</div></div></div>\n<p>Portsmouth has two cathedrals: the <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Cathedral" title="Portsmouth Cathedral">Anglican Cathedral of St Thomas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Old_Portsmouth" title="Old Portsmouth">Old Portsmouth</a>, and the Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_St_John_the_Evangelist,_Portsmouth" title="Cathedral of St John the Evangelist, Portsmouth">Cathedral of St John the Evangelist</a> (the city is one of 34 British settlements with a <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> cathedral).<sup id="cite_ref-cathhh_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cathhh-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s first chapel, dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Becket" title="Thomas Becket">Thomas Becket</a>, was built by Jean de<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Gisors in the second half of the 12th century.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chapel2_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chapel2-316">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> The chapel was rebuilt and developed into the <a href="/wiki/Parish_church" title="Parish church">parish church</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Cathedral" title="Portsmouth Cathedral">Anglican cathedral</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-chapel2_316-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chapel2-316">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> It was damaged during the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Portsmouth" title="Siege of Portsmouth">Siege of Portsmouth</a> in 1642, but after the restoration of the monarchy the tower and <a href="/wiki/Nave" title="Nave">nave</a> were rebuilt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKnowles200621_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKnowles200621-318">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> Significant changes were made when the Diocese of Portsmouth was established in 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201344_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201344-319">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> It became a cathedral in 1932, and was enlarged, although construction was halted during the Second World War. The cathedral was re-consecrated in the presence of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_The_Queen_Mother" title="Queen Elizabeth The Queen Mother">Queen Elizabeth The Queen Mother</a> in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Domus_Dei" title="Domus Dei">Royal Garrison Church</a> was founded in 1212 by <a href="/wiki/Peter_des_Roches" title="Peter des Roches">Peter des Roches</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Winchester" title="Bishop of Winchester">Bishop of Winchester</a>. After centuries of decay, it became an ammunition store in 1540. The marriage of Charles<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>II to Catherine of Braganza took place in the church in 1662. After the defeat of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leipzig" title="Battle of Leipzig">Battle of Leipzig</a> in 1814, large receptions were held inside the church. In 1941, a firebomb fell on the roof, destroying the nave.<sup id="cite_ref-garr_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-garr-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The church\'s chancel was saved by servicemen shortly after the raid; however, replacing the roof was determined to be impossible due to the large amounts of salt solution the stonework had absorbed over the years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013150_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt2013150-321">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Cathedral of St John the Evangelist was built in 1882 to accommodate Portsmouth\'s increasing Roman Catholic population, replacing a chapel built in 1796 to the west. Before 1791 Roman Catholic chapels in towns with <a href="/wiki/Borough_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Borough status in the United Kingdom">borough status</a> were prohibited. The chapel was opened after the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Relief_Act_1791" title="Roman Catholic Relief Act 1791">Roman Catholic Relief Act 1791</a> was passed and then replaced by the cathedral.<sup id="cite_ref-catholic_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-catholic-322">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> Its construction was completed in phases: in 1882 the nave was complete; in 1886 the crossing was finished, and the <a href="/wiki/Chancel" title="Chancel">chancel</a> was ready by 1893, eleven years after its opening. During the blitz, the cathedral was badly damaged when Luftwaffe bombing destroyed Bishop\'s House next door. It was restored in 1970, 1982, and 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-catholic_322-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-catholic-322">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Portsmouth" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Portsmouth">Roman Catholic Diocese of Portsmouth</a> was founded in 1882 by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_XIII" title="Pope Leo XIII">Pope Leo XIII</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Smaller places of worship in the city include St<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Jude\'s Church in Southsea,<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Church,_Portsea" title="St Mary&#39;s Church, Portsea">St<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Mary\'s Church</a> in Portsea,<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St_Ann%27s_Church,_HMNB_Portsmouth" title="St Ann&#39;s Church, HMNB Portsmouth">St<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Ann\'s Chapel</a> in the naval base<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_and_Southsea_Synagogue" title="Portsmouth and Southsea Synagogue">Portsmouth and Southsea Synagogue</a>, which is among the oldest <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogues</a> in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fratton_Park,_Sep_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Fratton Park football stadium at night, home to Portsmouth F.C. The pitch is lit by floodlights." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Fratton_Park%2C_Sep_2006.jpg/220px-Fratton_Park%2C_Sep_2006.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Fratton_Park%2C_Sep_2006.jpg/330px-Fratton_Park%2C_Sep_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Fratton_Park%2C_Sep_2006.jpg/440px-Fratton_Park%2C_Sep_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fratton_Park,_Sep_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fratton_Park" title="Fratton Park">Fratton Park</a>, home to <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth F.C.</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth F.C.</a> play their home games at <a href="/wiki/Fratton_Park" title="Fratton Park">Fratton Park</a>. They have won two <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a> titles (1949 and 1950)<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rsssf_330-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf-330">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup> and won the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1939_FA_Cup_Final" title="1939 FA Cup Final">1939</a> and <a href="/wiki/2008_FA_Cup_Final" title="2008 FA Cup Final">2008</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeasom198421_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeasom198421-331">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup> They returned to the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup> In 2010 they were relegated to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Championship</a>, and amid serious financial difficulties in February 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup> they were further relegated to <a href="/wiki/Football_League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League One">League One</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-shit_335-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shit-335">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> In 2013 Portsmouth were relegated again, this time placing them in the <a href="/wiki/League_Two" class="mw-redirect" title="League Two">League Two</a>, the fourth tier of English Football.<sup id="cite_ref-shit_335-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shit-335">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> In April 2013, Portsmouth<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>F.C. was purchased by the Pompey Supporters Trust, becoming the largest fan-owned football club in English Football history.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup> In May 2017, Portsmouth F.C. were promoted as League Two Champions to <a href="/wiki/League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="League One">League One</a> for the 2017-18 season.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Moneyfields_F.C." title="Moneyfields F.C.">Moneyfields F.C.</a> have been playing in the <a href="/wiki/Wessex_Football_League" title="Wessex Football League">Wessex Football League</a> Premier Division since 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_Services_Portsmouth_F.C." title="United Services Portsmouth F.C.">United Services Portsmouth F.C.</a> (formerly known as Portsmouth Royal Navy) and <a href="/wiki/Baffins_Milton_Rovers_F.C." title="Baffins Milton Rovers F.C.">Baffins Milton Rovers F.C.</a> both compete in Wessex League Division One, with United Services being formed in 1962,<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup> and Baffins Milton Rovers being founded in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby</a> teams, <a href="/wiki/United_Services_Portsmouth_Rugby_Football_Club" title="United Services Portsmouth Rugby Football Club">United Services Portsmouth RFC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy_Rugby_Union" title="Royal Navy Rugby Union">Royal Navy Rugby Union</a>, both play their home matches at the United Services Recreation Ground in the city. Royal Navy Rugby Union play in the annual <a href="/wiki/Army_Navy_Match" title="Army Navy Match">Army Navy Match</a> at <a href="/wiki/Twickenham" title="Twickenham">Twickenham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Portsmouth hosted <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class cricket</a> at the <a href="/wiki/United_Services_Recreation_Ground" title="United Services Recreation Ground">United Services Recreation Ground</a> from 1882,<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup> while from 1895 to 2000 <a href="/wiki/Hampshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Hampshire County Cricket Club">Hampshire County Cricket Club</a> matches were played there. This arrangement came to an end in 2000 when Hampshire moved all their home matches to their newly built <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_(cricket_ground)" title="Rose Bowl (cricket ground)">Rose Bowl</a> cricket ground in <a href="/wiki/West_End,_Hampshire" title="West End, Hampshire">West End</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PRO_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRO-343">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup> The city is also home to four <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">hockey</a> clubs: City of Portsmouth Hockey Club, who are based at the University\'s Langstone Campus;<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> Portsmouth &amp; Southsea Hockey Club, and Portsmouth Sharks Hockey Club, who are both based at the <a href="/wiki/Admiral_Lord_Nelson_School" title="Admiral Lord Nelson School">Admiral Lord Nelson School</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> and United Services Portsmouth Hockey Club, who are based on Burnaby Road.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> Great Salterns Golf Club, established in 1926,<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup> is an 18-hole parkland course with two holes playing across Saltern lake.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> There are also coastal courses at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hayling_Golf_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hayling Golf Club (page does not exist)">Hayling</a>, near the entrance to Langstone Harbour in the east and at the <a href="/wiki/Gosport_and_Stokes_Bay_Golf_Club" title="Gosport and Stokes Bay Golf Club">Gosport and Stokes Bay Golf Club</a> to the west of Portsmouth Harbour entrance in Gosport.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_114-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Boxing was a popular past time, particularly between 1910 and 1960, with a monument being erected in 2017 to commemorate the city\'s boxing heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_and_communications">Transport and communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transport and communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Buses_in_Portsmouth" title="Buses in Portsmouth">Buses in Portsmouth</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_busy_scene_with_ferries_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1306443.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A view of various ferries, cargo and military vessels moving out of Portsmouth Harbour. This photograph was taken from the viewing deck of the Spinnaker Tower." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/A_busy_scene_with_ferries_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1306443.jpg/220px-A_busy_scene_with_ferries_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1306443.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/A_busy_scene_with_ferries_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1306443.jpg/330px-A_busy_scene_with_ferries_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1306443.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/A_busy_scene_with_ferries_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1306443.jpg/440px-A_busy_scene_with_ferries_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1306443.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_busy_scene_with_ferries_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1306443.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ferries, cargo and military vessels operating from Portsmouth Harbour</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ferries">Ferries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ferries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Portsmouth Harbour has passenger ferry links to <a href="/wiki/Gosport" title="Gosport">Gosport</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_International_Port" title="Portsmouth International Port">Portsmouth International Port</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup> with a car ferry service to the Isle of Wight operated by <a href="/wiki/Wightlink" title="Wightlink">Wightlink</a> located nearby.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup> Britain\'s longest-standing commercial <a href="/wiki/Hovercraft" title="Hovercraft">hovercraft</a> service, begun in the 1960s, still runs from near Clarence Pier to <a href="/wiki/Ryde" title="Ryde">Ryde</a>, Isle of Wight, operated by <a href="/wiki/Hovertravel" title="Hovertravel">Hovertravel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup> Portsmouth Continental Ferry Port has links to <a href="/wiki/Caen" title="Caen">Caen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cherbourg-Octeville" title="Cherbourg-Octeville">Cherbourg-Octeville</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Malo" class="mw-redirect" title="St Malo">St Malo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Le_Havre" title="Le Havre">Le Havre</a> in France,<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Santander,_Cantabria" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander, Cantabria">Santander</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a> in Spain,<sup id="cite_ref-bit_355-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bit-355">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-chan_356-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chan-356">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup> Ferry services from the port are operated by <a href="/wiki/Brittany_Ferries" title="Brittany Ferries">Brittany Ferries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Condor_Ferries" title="Condor Ferries">Condor Ferries</a>, and <a href="/wiki/LD_Lines" title="LD Lines">LD Lines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bit_355-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bit-355">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 May 2006, <a href="/wiki/Trasmediterranea" class="mw-redirect" title="Trasmediterranea">Trasmediterranea</a> started a service to Bilbao in competition with <a href="/wiki/P%26O_Ferries" title="P&amp;O Ferries">P&amp;O</a>\'s then-existing service. This service was criticised when the ferry <i>Fortuny</i> was detained in Portsmouth by the <a href="/wiki/Maritime_and_Coastguard_Agency" title="Maritime and Coastguard Agency">Maritime and Coastguard Agency</a> for numerous safety breaches.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup> The faults were quickly corrected by Trasmediterr\xc3\xa1nea, and the service was cleared to begin carrying passengers on 23 May 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> In March 2007, Trasmediterr\xc3\xa1nea withdrew the Bilbao service at short notice, citing the need to deploy the <i>Fortuny</i> elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup> P&amp;O Ferries ceased their service to <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a> on 27 September 2010, due to "unsustainable losses".<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup> The port is the second-busiest ferry port in the UK after <a href="/wiki/Dover" title="Dover">Dover</a>, handling around three million passengers a year.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">Buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Buses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Local bus services are provided by <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_South_East" title="Stagecoach South East">Stagecoach</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_Hampshire_%26_Dorset" title="First Hampshire &amp; Dorset">First Hampshire &amp; Dorset</a>, serving the city of Portsmouth and its surrounding towns. Hovertravel and Stagecoach run a bus service called the Hoverbus from the city centre to Southsea Hovercraft Terminal and <a href="/wiki/The_Hard_Interchange" class="mw-redirect" title="The Hard Interchange">The Hard Interchange</a>, near the seafront.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Countryliner runs a Saturday service to <a href="/wiki/Midhurst" title="Midhurst">Midhurst</a> in West Sussex,<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Xelabus" title="Xelabus">Xelabus</a> operate a Sunday open-top seafront summer service around the city as of  2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express</a> services from Portsmouth run mainly from The Hard Interchange to <a href="/wiki/London_Victoria_station" title="London Victoria station">London Victoria station</a>, Cornwall, <a href="/wiki/Bradford" title="Bradford">Bradford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birkenhead" title="Birkenhead">Birkenhead</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railways">Railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The city has several mainline railway stations, including <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_%26_Southsea_railway_station" title="Portsmouth &amp; Southsea railway station">Portsmouth &amp; Southsea railway station</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Harbour_railway_station" title="Portsmouth Harbour railway station">Portsmouth Harbour railway station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup> Portsmouth lies on two different direct <a href="/wiki/South_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="South Western Railway (train operating company)">South Western Railway</a> routes to <a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Waterloo railway station">London Waterloo</a>, via <a href="/wiki/Guildford_(Surrey)_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Guildford (Surrey) railway station">Guildford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basingstoke_railway_station" title="Basingstoke railway station">Basingstoke</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup> There is also a South Western Railway stopping service to Southampton Central and a service by <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="Great Western Railway (train operating company)">Great Western Railway</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Central_railway_station" title="Cardiff Central railway station">Cardiff Central</a> via Southampton, <a href="/wiki/Salisbury_railway_station" title="Salisbury railway station">Salisbury</a>, Bath, and Bristol.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Southern_(train_operating_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern (train operating company)">Southern</a> additionally offers service to <a href="/wiki/Brighton_railway_station" title="Brighton railway station">Brighton</a>, Gatwick Airport, <a href="/wiki/East_Croydon_station" title="East Croydon station">Croydon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/London_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Victoria railway station">London Victoria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Airport_(Hampshire)" title="Portsmouth Airport (Hampshire)">Portsmouth Airport</a>, an airport with a grass runway, was in operation from 1932 to 1973. After its closure, housing (Anchorage Park), industrial sites, retail stores (Ocean Retail Park), and a school (Admiral Lord Nelson School) were built on the site.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup> Today, the nearest airport is <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Airport" title="Southampton Airport">Southampton Airport</a>, situated in the <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Eastleigh" title="Borough of Eastleigh">Borough of Eastleigh</a>, which lies 19.8 miles (31.9&#160;km) away.<sup id="cite_ref-GM_114-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GM-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The airport has an indirect <a href="/wiki/South_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="South Western Railway (train operating company)">South Western Railway</a> rail connection requiring a change at <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Central_railway_station" title="Southampton Central railway station">Southampton Central</a> or <a href="/wiki/Eastleigh_railway_station" title="Eastleigh railway station">Eastleigh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick</a> are 65 miles (105&#160;km) and 75 miles (121&#160;km) away, respectively. Gatwick is directly linked by Southern train services to London Victoria station, while Heathrow is linked by coach to <a href="/wiki/Woking" title="Woking">Woking</a>, which is on both rail lines to <a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo" class="mw-redirect" title="London Waterloo">London Waterloo</a>, or by <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup> Heathrow is directly linked to Portsmouth by National Express coaches.<sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_public_transport_projects">Possible public transport projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Possible public transport projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There is an ongoing debate on the development of a new public transport structure, with <a href="/wiki/Monorail" title="Monorail">monorails</a> and <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> both being considered. A light rail link to Gosport was authorised in 2002 with completion expected in 2005, but it is unlikely that the project will be completed following the refusal of funding by the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> in November 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup> In April 2011, an article appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/The_News_(Portsmouth)" title="The News (Portsmouth)">Portsmouth News</a></i> suggesting a new scheme could be in the offing by running a light rapid transit system over the line to Southampton via Fareham, <a href="/wiki/Bursledon" title="Bursledon">Bursledon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sholing" title="Sholing">Sholing</a>, thus replacing the existing heavy rail services.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">&#91;379&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Portsmouth, along with Southampton and its adjacent towns, are served predominantly with transmissions from the <a href="/wiki/Rowridge_Transmitter" class="mw-redirect" title="Rowridge Transmitter">Rowridge Transmitter</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a><sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">&#91;380&#93;</a></sup>, though the transmitter at <a href="/wiki/Midhurst_transmitting_station" title="Midhurst transmitting station">Midhurst</a> can provide a subsitute for Rowridge.  Portsmouth was one of the first cities in the UK to have a local TV station, MyTV; although the Isle of Wight had a local television service which began broadcasting in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">&#91;381&#93;</a></sup> In November 2014, a new TV station, named <a href="/wiki/That%27s_Solent" title="That&#39;s Solent">That\'s Solent</a>, was launched as part of a nationwide roll-out of local Freeview channels in south central England.<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup> The stations are broadcast from the Rowridge Transmitter on the <a href="/wiki/Isle_Of_Wight" class="mw-redirect" title="Isle Of Wight">Isle Of Wight</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">&#91;383&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The local commercial radio station is <a href="/wiki/The_Breeze_(radio_network)" title="The Breeze (radio network)">The Breeze</a> on 107.4FM,<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup> while the city also has a non-profit community radio station <a href="/wiki/Express_FM" title="Express FM">Express FM</a> on 93.7FM.<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">&#91;385&#93;</a></sup> Patients at Portsmouth\'s primary hospital, <a href="/wiki/Queen_Alexandra_Hospital" title="Queen Alexandra Hospital">Queen Alexandra</a> in Milton, also have access to local programming from charity station Portsmouth Hospital Broadcasting, which starting broadcasting in 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">&#91;386&#93;</a></sup> When the first local commercial radio stations were licensed in the 1970s by the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Broadcasting_Authority" title="Independent Broadcasting Authority">Independent Broadcasting Authority</a> (IBA), <a href="/wiki/Radio_Victory" title="Radio Victory">Radio Victory</a> was the radio service for Portsmouth. In 1986, due to transmission area changes by the IBA, it was replaced by a new company and service called Ocean Sound, later renamed as <a href="/wiki/Heart_Hampshire" title="Heart Hampshire">Heart Hampshire</a>. From the city\'s 800th birthday in 1994, Victory<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>FM broadcast for three 28-day periods over an 18-month period.<sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">&#91;387&#93;</a></sup> It was purchased from the founders by TLRC, who, due to poor <a href="/wiki/RAJAR" title="RAJAR">RAJAR</a> figures, relaunched the service in 2001 as Ocean FM,<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">&#91;388&#93;</a></sup> with Portsmouth Football Club purchasing a stake in the station during 2007 and selling it in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">&#91;389&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city currently has one daily local newspaper known as <i><a href="/wiki/The_News_(Portsmouth)" title="The News (Portsmouth)">The News</a></i>. The paper was established in 1873 and was previously known as the <i>Portsmouth Evening News</i>. A free weekly newspaper is published by the same publisher, <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Press" title="Johnston Press">Johnston Press</a>, called <i>The Journal</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">&#91;390&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">&#91;391&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_residents">Notable residents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Notable residents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Portsmouth" title="List of people from Portsmouth">List of people from Portsmouth</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Southsea_War_Memorial_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1297412.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The Naval War Memorial in Southsea, which consists of a large stone pillar and a plaque at the bottom which commemorates the fallen soldiers of the Second World War." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Southsea_War_Memorial_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1297412.jpg/170px-Southsea_War_Memorial_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1297412.jpg" width="170" height="301" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Southsea_War_Memorial_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1297412.jpg/255px-Southsea_War_Memorial_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1297412.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Southsea_War_Memorial_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1297412.jpg/340px-Southsea_War_Memorial_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1297412.jpg 2x" data-file-width="361" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Southsea_War_Memorial_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1297412.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Naval War Memorial in Southsea</div></div></div>\n<p>The city has been home to a number of famed authors. Most notably <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 known for such works as <i><a href="/wiki/Oliver_Twist" title="Oliver Twist">Oliver Twist</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Tale_of_Two_Cities" title="A Tale of Two Cities">A Tale of Two Cities</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pickwick_Papers" title="The Pickwick Papers">The Pickwick Papers</a></i>&#160;&#8211;&#32;was born in Portsmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-395" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-395">&#91;392&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Conan_Doyle" title="Arthur Conan Doyle">Arthur Conan Doyle</a>, author of the <a href="/wiki/Sherlock_Holmes" title="Sherlock Holmes">Sherlock Holmes</a> stories, practised as a doctor in the city and played in goal for Portsmouth Association Football Club, an amateur team not to be confused with the later professional Portsmouth Football Club.<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">&#91;393&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">&#91;394&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rudyard_Kipling" title="Rudyard Kipling">Rudyard Kipling</a>, poet and author of the <i><a href="/wiki/Jungle_Book" class="mw-redirect" title="Jungle Book">Jungle Book</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-blue_398-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blue-398">&#91;395&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/H._G._Wells" title="H. G. Wells">H. G. Wells</a>, author of <i><a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Worlds" class="mw-redirect" title="War of the Worlds">War of the Worlds</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Time_Machine" title="The Time Machine">The Time Machine</a></i>, lived in Portsmouth during the 1880s.<sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-399">&#91;396&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sir_Walter_Besant" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Walter Besant">Sir Walter Besant</a>, a novelist and historian, was born in Portsmouth,<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup> writing one novel set exclusively in the town, <i>By Celia\'s Arbour, A Tale of Portsmouth Town</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">&#91;398&#93;</a></sup> Historian <a href="/wiki/Frances_Yates" title="Frances Yates">Frances Yates</a> was born in Portsmouth and is known for her work on Renaissance <a href="/wiki/Western_esotericism" title="Western esotericism">esotericism</a>. Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Austen" title="Francis Austen">Francis Austen</a>, brother of <a href="/wiki/Jane_Austen" title="Jane Austen">Jane Austen</a>, briefly lived in the area after graduating from Portsmouth Naval Academy.<sup id="cite_ref-402" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-402">&#91;399&#93;</a></sup> More contemporary Portsmouth literary figures include social critic, journalist, and author <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Hitchens" title="Christopher Hitchens">Christopher Hitchens</a>, who was born in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-403" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-403">&#91;400&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nevil_Shute" title="Nevil Shute">Nevil Shute</a> moved to Portsmouth in 1934 when he relocated his aircraft company to the city; his former home stands in Southsea.<sup id="cite_ref-404" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-404">&#91;401&#93;</a></sup> Fantasy author <a href="/wiki/Neil_Gaiman" title="Neil Gaiman">Neil Gaiman</a> grew up in nearby Purbrook and the Portsmouth suburb of Southsea, and in 2013 had a Southsea road named after his novel <i>The Ocean At The End Of The Lane</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-405" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-405">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Olivia_Manning" title="Olivia Manning">Olivia Manning</a>\'s childhood was also spent in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-406" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-406">&#91;403&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Isambard_Kingdom_Brunel" title="Isambard Kingdom Brunel">Isambard Kingdom Brunel</a>, a famed engineer of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, was born in Portsmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-407" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-407">&#91;404&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-408" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-408">&#91;405&#93;</a></sup> His father <a href="/wiki/Marc_Isambard_Brunel" title="Marc Isambard Brunel">Marc Isambard Brunel</a> worked for the Royal Navy and invented the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Production_line" title="Production line">production line</a> to mass manufacture <a href="/wiki/Block_(sailing)" title="Block (sailing)">pulley blocks</a> for the rigging in Royal Navy vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-royal_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-royal-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Callaghan" title="James Callaghan">James Callaghan</a>, who was British prime minister from 1976 to 1979, was born and raised in Portsmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-409" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-409">&#91;406&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">&#91;407&#93;</a></sup> He was the son of a Protestant Northern Irish petty officer in the Royal Navy and was also the only person to have held all four <a href="/wiki/Great_Offices_of_State" title="Great Offices of State">Great Offices of State</a>, having previously served as Foreign Secretary, Home Secretary, and Chancellor.<sup id="cite_ref-411" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-411">&#91;408&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Pounds" title="John Pounds">John Pounds</a>, the founder of the <a href="/wiki/Ragged_school" title="Ragged school">ragged school</a>, which provided free education to working class children, lived in Portsmouth and set up the country\'s first ragged school in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-412" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-412">&#91;409&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sellers" title="Peter Sellers">Peter Sellers</a>, comedian, actor, and performer, was born in Southsea,<sup id="cite_ref-413" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-413">&#91;410&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a> lived and trained in Portsmouth for a short time.<sup id="cite_ref-414" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-414">&#91;411&#93;</a></sup> Several other professional actors have also been born, or lived, in the city, including; <i><a href="/wiki/EastEnders" title="EastEnders">EastEnders</a></i> actress <a href="/wiki/Emma_Barton" title="Emma Barton">Emma Barton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-415" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-415">&#91;412&#93;</a></sup> and Bollywood actress <a href="/wiki/Geeta_Basra" title="Geeta Basra">Geeta Basra</a>, who originally hails from Portsmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-416" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-416">&#91;413&#93;</a></sup> Cryptozoologist <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Downes" title="Jonathan Downes">Jonathan Downes</a> was born and lived in Portsmouth for a time.<sup id="cite_ref-417" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-417">&#91;414&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Helen_Duncan" title="Helen Duncan">Helen Duncan</a>, the last person to be imprisoned under the 1735 Witchcraft Act in the UK, was arrested in Portsmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-418" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-418">&#91;415&#93;</a></sup> Also new ly joined to the <a href="/wiki/EastEnders" title="EastEnders">Eastenders</a> cast Lorraine <a href="/wiki/Lorraine_Stanley" title="Lorraine Stanley">Stanley</a> was born and raised in Portsmouth.\n</p><p>Notable sportspeople from Portsmouth include <a href="/wiki/Michael_East_(athlete)" title="Michael East (athlete)">Michael East</a>, a Commonwealth Games gold medal-winning athlete,<sup id="cite_ref-419" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-419">&#91;416&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rob_Hayles" title="Rob Hayles">Rob Hayles</a>, cyclist and Olympic Games medal winner,<sup id="cite_ref-420" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-420">&#91;417&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tony_Oakey" title="Tony Oakey">Tony Oakey</a>, former British light-heavyweight boxing champion,<sup id="cite_ref-421" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-421">&#91;418&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Alan_Pascoe" title="Alan Pascoe">Alan Pascoe</a>, an Olympic medallist.<sup id="cite_ref-422" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-422">&#91;419&#93;</a></sup> Sir <a href="/wiki/Alec_Rose" title="Alec Rose">Alec Rose</a>, single-handed yachtsman,<sup id="cite_ref-423" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-423">&#91;420&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Katy_Sexton" title="Katy Sexton">Katy Sexton</a>, former world champion swimmer who won gold in the 200 metres (660&#160;ft) backstroke at the <a href="/wiki/2003_World_Aquatics_Championships" title="2003 World Aquatics Championships">2003 World Aquatics Championships</a> in Barcelona,<sup id="cite_ref-424" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-424">&#91;421&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Roger_Black" title="Roger Black">Roger Black</a>, an Olympic medallist, were also born in Portsmouth.<sup id="cite_ref-425" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-425">&#91;422&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="" and sister cities in the United Kingdom</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-130"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-130">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">These were part of a network of fortifications intended to guard military bases on the British coastline from an inland attack. They were built in the 19th century under the orders of Lord Palmerston.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHewitt201379_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHewitt201379-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-158"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-158">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Portsmouth is one of 34 British towns and cities with a Catholic cathedral.<sup id="cite_ref-cathhh_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cathhh-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-324"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-324">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Vatican policy in England at the time was to found <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">sees</a> in locations other than those used for Anglican cathedrals.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portsmouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<dl><dt>Citations</dt></dl>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
